  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer16777115161033490252">Grace Divine, daughter of the local pastor, always knew something terrible happened the night Daniel Kalbi disappeared--the night she found her brother Jude collapsed on the porch, covered in his own blood--but she has no idea what a truly monstrous secret that night held.<br/><br/>The memories her family has tried to bury resurface when Daniel returns, three years later, and enroll</span>
  <span id="freeText16777115161033490252" style="display:none">Grace Divine, daughter of the local pastor, always knew something terrible happened the night Daniel Kalbi disappeared--the night she found her brother Jude collapsed on the porch, covered in his own blood--but she has no idea what a truly monstrous secret that night held.<br /><br />The memories her family has tried to bury resurface when Daniel returns, three years later, and enrolls in Grace and Jude's high school. Despite promising Jude she'll stay away, Grace cannot deny her attraction to Daniel's shocking artistic abilities, his way of getting her to look at the world from new angles, and the strange, hungry glint in his eyes.<br /><br />The closer Grace gets to Daniel, the more she jeopardizes her life, as her actions stir resentment in Jude and drive him to embrace the ancient evil Daniel unleashed that horrific night. Grace must discover the truth behind the boy's dark secret...and the cure that can save the ones she loves. But she may have to lay down the ultimate sacrifice to do it--her soul.</span>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Look, dude. These people commenting aren't telling you the truth. Here it is: it all boils down to a matter of preference.<br/><br/>For example, do you seek a b<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Look, dude. These people commenting aren't telling you the truth. Here it is: it all boils down to a matter of preference.<br /><br />For example, do you seek a book that's full of cliches and is a watered-down version of a watered-down version of a watered-down version? Then this book may be right up your alley. <br /><br />If, however, you are anything like me, you will want something at least slightly original, interesting, enjoyable and filled with some amount of depth. If that's the case, run far away from this book. Of course, you asked this question 4 years ago, so I'm assuming you've decided by now.<br /><br />Does no one know how to give an honest answer these days?<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/97975691" />
    <a title="Megan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1233686-megan"><img alt="Megan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1334791106p2/1233686.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/97975691?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Megan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Megan" href="/user/show/1233686-megan">Megan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1233686-megan?shelf=not-mine-library">not-mine-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1233686-megan?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1233686-megan?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1233686-megan?shelf=did-not-finish">did-not-finish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer97975691" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11803934044232071504">I am not going to hide this review under a "contains spoilers" warning, because only a very young reader completely unaware of the current trend towards paranormal fiction or a severely mentally disabled person would not figure out the big mystery when, on page 64, Daniel "<b>barks</b>" at Grace when he invites her into his room and she makes the observation that, "<b>It looked like someone had been keeping a large dog in this closet/room. The door was marred by several claw-like gashes - like the way Dai</b></span>
  <span id="freeText11803934044232071504" style="display:none">I am not going to hide this review under a "contains spoilers" warning, because only a very young reader completely unaware of the current trend towards paranormal fiction or a severely mentally disabled person would not figure out the big mystery when, on page 64, Daniel "<b>barks</b>" at Grace when he invites her into his room and she makes the observation that, "<b>It looked like someone had been keeping a large dog in this closet/room. The door was marred by several claw-like gashes - like the way Daisy would leave scratches on my bedroom door when I left her home alone, only these scratches were much larger and deeper. Whatever animal had been kept in here had apparently gotten out</b>." A page later, Grace remarks that Daniel looks, "<b>like a starved dog</b>." <br /><br /><i>The Dark Divine</i> is filled with growls, howls, yelps ~ and even less subtle hints. Yet our protagonist, Grace Divine, doesn't figure out the mystery until she is very blatantly told on page 236. Upon <s>discovering</s> being told the supernatural secret of her childhood friend and long time crush Grace rushes home and.... at this point, I have to interrupt to say that I would be questioning my beliefs, the world I live in, and possibly past episodes of <a href="http://www.xfiles.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">The X-Files</a> and <a href="http://www.coasttocoastam.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Coast to Coast AM</a>. But Grace, upon learning that mystical beasts do exist, simply runs home and <i>blames herself</i>. <s>Daniel</s> Mr. Long Time Crush told her that his, er... condition is hereditary. Grace is a high school junior currently enrolled in a chemistry ~ she had to have taken biology to have gotten that far. So she should understand about complicated things such as genes, yes? Yet she spends the following morning crying and reflects, <br /><br /><b>...mostly I sobbed for what I now knew about myself.<br />I felt like such a fraud. My father told me my name meant mercy, help, and guidance. But he was wrong. All Grace Divine meant was blundering, meddling, disappointment. Everything I touched - everything I tried to help - fell apart and slipped through my fingers. <br />Why did I have to press the issue, refuse to stay ignorant? Why couldn't I stop myself from creating this mess?<br />If I had just stayed out of things, if I had just minded my own business for all these years, would everything be the way it used to? Would Daniel still be the blondhaired boy next door...</b><br /><br />I gave up on this one a few pages after reading the above pity party. Seriously, when someone tells you they have an unwanted <i>genetic</i> condition, what sort of person runs home and blames herself??? Unless of course you are the parent ;) But if you're not the parent... then how fucking self-absorbed does that make you?<br /><br />Granted, the majority of my reasons for disliking this book are personal ~ I am much older than the target audience and as such, the surprises aren't actually surprises and the plot is incredibly formulaic. As someone who spent my teen years rebelling as much as possible (including rebelling against my Catholic schooling by discovering atheism) I simply cannot relate the pastor's daughter and perpetual good-girl Grace Divine. Not only does she obey all of her parents rules, she doesn't even question them ~ even when her parents rules are in direct conflict with what she desires. Not that I'm endorsing all teens to pull an <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=lZLVi4v7lSM" rel="nofollow noopener">Eric Cartman</a>, but I do expect some independent thought. Speaking of which, Grace is the worst excuse for a heroine since Bella Swan. Actually, I believe I hate Grace a little bit more than Bella. Grace doesn't figure out anything for herself and frequently takes "no" for an answer when she questions Daniel, her dad and her brother as she blunders her way through this book. <br /><br />My final reasons for disliking <i>The Dark Divine</i> are incredibly petty, but worth mentioning simply so I can get them off my chest:<br />~I felt cheated by the cover. Yes, I know that covers are ridiculously misleading. But this one is so pretty, and a little sex-ay. Although I quit on page 263 (out of 372) I am certain that the book will not live up to the cover. <br />~The font appears to be <b>bold</b> and, as many others have pointed out, incredibly irritating to read.<br /><br />Despite the above gripes, the bottom line is that her story bugged me, so I am done.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11803934044232071504" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_155940031" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/155940031" />
    <a title="Lea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5152540-lea"><img alt="Lea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1341265725p2/5152540.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/155940031?book_show_action=true">Mar 22, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lea" href="/user/show/5152540-lea">Lea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5152540-lea?shelf=made-me-want-to-punch-something">made-me-want-to-punch-something</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5152540-lea?shelf=murder-mystery">murder-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5152540-lea?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5152540-lea?shelf=tstl-heroines">tstl-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5152540-lea?shelf=love-triangle">love-triangle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5152540-lea?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5152540-lea?shelf=make-it-stop-now">make-it-stop-now</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5152540-lea?shelf=epic-fail">epic-fail</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5152540-lea?shelf=lazy-writing">lazy-writing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5152540-lea?shelf=high-school-drama-fest">high-school-drama-fest</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer155940031" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10830466031660826120"><div>
  <br/>
  <a href='http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-m7QUvOX98DM/Ue_W7D0kD9I/AAAAAAAAEuY/NPoyirtc3J0/s1600/grumpy+cat.jpeg' rel='nofollow noopener'>
    <img height='320' src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380347303i/701649.jpg' width='258' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
  </a>
</div><br/><br/>No, no, a thousand flipping times <i>NO</i>.<br/><br/>I just don't get it. Like, <i>how</i> do books like this even make it to publishing when they are two steps away from being misogynistic/religious propaganda at worst and brain-numbing fluff at best? And yet once again, I was totally and completely struck silly by the ZOMG GORGEOUS COVER and thought hey, with a cover like that, how could it be *that* bad?<br/><br/>I really need to start learning.<br/><br/>So, here is basically what<i> The Dark Divine </i>is about, since having </span>
  <span id="freeText10830466031660826120" style="display:none"><div>
  <br>
  <a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-m7QUvOX98DM/Ue_W7D0kD9I/AAAAAAAAEuY/NPoyirtc3J0/s1600/grumpy+cat.jpeg" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img height="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380347303i/701649.jpg" width="258" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</div><br><br>No, no, a thousand flipping times <i>NO</i>.<br><br>I just don't get it. Like, <i>how</i> do books like this even make it to publishing when they are two steps away from being misogynistic/religious propaganda at worst and brain-numbing fluff at best? And yet once again, I was totally and completely struck silly by the ZOMG GORGEOUS COVER and thought hey, with a cover like that, how could it be *that* bad?<br><br>I really need to start learning.<br><br>So, here is basically what<i> The Dark Divine </i>is about, since having not done too much research on it beforehand, I was sort of clueless myself. When I first started reading, I actually thought this was going to be a fallen angel book, , mainly because the religious overtones are so heavy-handed that they left me with bruises. But I digress...<br><br>Grace Divine is the local pastor's daughter, in her junior year of high school, whose world is turned upside down when Daniel Kalbi steps back into her life. Daniel is Grace's old childhood friend-- except that he mysteriously disappeared years ago after some horrible incident that happened with her older brother Jude. Now Grace's entire family basically pretends that Daniel no longer exists because of whatever terrible thing he did in the past. Obviously, our young heroine cannot stay away from this dark, brooding, and sardonic piece of man candy, and so begins our nearly 400-page whine-and-pine-fest between Grace Divine and Daniel Kalbi. The plot thickens when we later learn that Daniel is actually an <i>Urbat</i>, or "Dog of Death," cursed for past sins by God to be-- for lack of a better term-- a werewolf.<br><br>OK, werewolves, sweet, so this is a book about werewolves-- sounds pretty awesome! Except that it's<i> not</i>. Let me explain why:<br><br><b>Grace Divine</b><br><b>
  <br>
</b> Grace Divine. Where do I even begin with Grace Divine...<br><br>Well, for starters, she has one of THE most stuck-up and pretentious POV's I've ever had to suffer reading through. Now you would <i>think</i> that-- being the pastor's daughter-- we could maybe get some really interesting, super-cool and edgy character who likes to rebel against the system. But no. True to her name, Grace is a walking, talking Bible in knee-length skirt and loafers who never bothers to even <i>question</i> the rules her dogmatic parents lay down. Her day consists of trying her very best to be perfect and the rest of the time feeling guilty for not being absolutely perfect. Her religious thought process is enough to make you want to hurl your breakfast, while she reminds us <i>ad nauseam</i> of what a good little Christian girl she is, and by the way, you'd better be too, or you're going to BURN IN HELL.<br><br>No, I'm not making this up-- the entire book reads like a freaking fire-and-brimstone church sermon.<br><br>As if this wasn't enough to make me want to slap her silly, Grace also treats her friends like minions. I mean, she compares her best friend April to a dog in the very first paragraph of the book, and then compares her to a dog <i>again</i> about 30 pages later. Hmm, that's not very nice, is it? In fact, she spends the ENTIRE BOOK comparing her so-called best friend to various dogs. Not only is this really weird, this is pretty freaking terrible if you ask me. And yes, <i>thank you</i> Bree, I understood all the dog references, but really you didn't need to shove them down our throats JUST because your book is about werewolves. This whole dog comparison thing just made Grace look like an asshole. I honestly felt so bad for April. Who cares that she's sort of ditzy and clueless? Why does that give Grace the right to sit there in total disdain, comparing her to a dog? Screw that: April rocks, Grace is a stuck-up bitch who doesn't deserve to have friends because she doesn't give a crap about anyone but herself.<br><br>Grace also likes to repeatedly tell us how "smart" she is. After all, she has a 3.8 GPA, but unfortunately this doesn't give her the brains to stay away from someone as dangerously abusive as Daniel Kalbi. Everything she thinks, does and says makes you wonder how anyone can, in fact, be <i>that</i> big of a dumbass. Oh, and she also thinks that people who cry are weak. Yeah. I'm sorry, but you are going to be hard-pressed getting me to a like a main character who has a pole <i>thi</i>s far up her rear-end.<br><br>Bottom line- this is not a character I want to read about. This is a character I want to punch in the face for being so unbelievably stuck-up, self-absorbed, and let's not forget: <i>totally moronic</i>.<br><br><div>
  <br>
  <a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-KkzpNZo0BS8/UeFpJYibFeI/AAAAAAAAEro/_KEbE_XvAEI/s1600/stewie+gif.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img height="240" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380347303ra/701650.gif" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</div><br><br><b>
  <br>
</b> <b>Daniel Kalbi</b><br><b>
  <br>
</b> Hey there, boys and girls, how about another abusive and controlling relationship with a domineering male lead who keeps his cowering, brow-beaten woman on a leash? Alrighty then, fantastic!<br><br>Enter: Daniel Kalbi. Prime specimen of a condescending, ass-face love interest if I ever did see one, who treats our doe-eyed virginal Grace Divine as though she were a pile of dog poo he accidentally stepped in. Oh, Daniel, how I want to kick you in the crotch. Repeatedly.<br><b>
  <br>
</b> Let me give you a prime example of what a tool bag Daniel is: At one point in the story, Grace's car breaks down in a really bad section of town at night, and Pete (the required third wheel in the YA love triangle who is two steps away from being completely brain-dead), leaves her in the car because she'll be "safer" there. Alone in the car, Grace hears scratching outside- and then something starts rattling the car. Understandably <i>scared shitless</i>, she's relieved when she looks out the window and sees Daniel. Now get this: Frightened half to death, Grace asks Daniel if he saw anything that could have made the noises she heard-- She's trying to figure out what's going on after being in a potentially threatening situation that has left her shaken and upset... His reply? "Maybe."<br><br><i>MAYBE??!?!???</i><br> <br><div>
  <br>
  <a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-hQ50Hqzp_iI/Ud3vORNDdoI/AAAAAAAAErY/X6_WDwpB4xA/s1600/bridesmaids.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img height="148" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380347303ra/701651.gif" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</div><br><br><br>Congratulations Daniel, you have officially been inaugurated into my YA Douchebag Hall of Fame.<br><br>Oh, and did I mention that any time Grace asks something from Daniel, he says "Kiss me"? Yeah, so.. basically if Grace wants anything from Daniel she is asked to essentially whore herself out to get it. Of course, Grace being Grace, she acts all disoriented and confused whenever he says this, instead of doing the logical thing and telling him to go light himself on fire and jump off a cliff.<br><br>I'm going to take a deep breath at this point, so that I don't once again hurl this book across my room, or suffer from a massive brain implosion. The level of disrespect and disgusting apathy shown by this pathetic excuse for a human being is not even worth my time. I just. I can't even. I'm done.<br><br>(OH. And also- about half-way through the book we're given<i> reasons</i> that try to excuse Daniel for his awful behavior. I'm sorry, but this is BS. I don't care about your troubled past, or your dumb curse, you don't treat people like this. EVER. <i>END OF STORY.</i>)<br><br><br><b>Blatant push of Christian agenda in a YA book</b><br><b>
  <br>
</b> Oh sweet baby Jesus, the religious overtones in this book. If you enjoy being whacked over the head with the New Testament until you're semi-unconscious, then this is the book for you. Grace Divine's dad-- a pastor, go figure-- was one big judgmental and pretentious douchebag who everyone calls "an angel of the Lord." OK, can I just say something here? If you want to write a book where your main characters are Christians, fine. But don't make those main characters Puritanical religious-as-fudge jerk-wads in an attempt to sneak in some kind of hidden agenda and then put that ish into a YA book. Also, I know Christians. They don't effing talk like they just stepped out of 17th century Salem, alrighty? And not all of them think and act like they have heavenly beams shining out of their bums. The way Bree writes about them just perpetuates the idea that all Christians are supposed to be self-important pricks with delusions of being "holier than thou," and even more messed up, that this is actually a GOOD thing. Welp, that is absolute B.S. and I'm calling it out as being such.<br><b>
  <br>
</b> <b>Useless facts that have nothing to do with anything</b><br><b>
  <br>
</b>Here is a prime example of the inconsequential and totally boring pieces of info the reader has to suffer through in this book:<br><br><i>"Got any more of that tea?" Dad asked...</i><br><i>
  <br>
</i><i>"Um, yeah." I mopped up the puddle I'd spilled on the counter. "It's chamomile though."</i><br><i>
  <br>
</i><i>Dad crinkled his Rodulph nose.</i><br><i>
  <br>
</i><i>"I think I saw some peppermint in the cupboard. I'll get it for you."</i><br><br>OK, so you probably don't want to listen to me nitpick, but gosh darn it, I'm gonna nitpick. Why? Because this <u>entire book</u> is chock FULL of completely mindless/useless interactions like this one.<br><br>I'm sorry Bree, but what the flying fig newton does Grace's dad not liking chamomile have to do with, oh I don't know... <i>ANYTHING??</i> It has nothing to do with the plot, it adds nada to any character development, and it's not even <i>remotely</i> interesting. Please tell me why I should care that Grace's dad doesn't like chamomile tea? No reason? OK, so what is the POINT of putting it in the book?? Answer: There IS none, it's just there as empty-- not to mention seriously boring-- filler to an already shallow story. So.... yeah, Grace's dad doesn't like chamomile, Maryanne Duke makes the best rhubarb pie EVER, Carolyn Bordeaux has something to do with the angel memorial... I have a pretty high threshold for pointless filler, but this is just getting stupid.<br><br><div>
  <br>
  <a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-39XafoGzaYU/UeFpTUhHKxI/AAAAAAAAErw/6JKo6_bjq6U/s1600/jenna+look+at+all+the+fucks+i+give.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img height="193" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380347303ra/701652.gif" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</div><br><br><br><b>Can I have some cheese with that dialogue?</b><br> <br>Speaking of things that make me want to gauge my eyes out with a rusty spoon, we also have some of the most atrocious dialogue ever. Lord have mercy, the dialogue. It was painful. Basically, it reads like a bunch of teenagers talking the way a 40-year old woman thinks youngins talk-- If they were in a squeaky-clean Christian production of <i>Get Thee to the Church Unless Ye Longeth to Burn in Hell</i>. I'd give examples, but at this point I'm just too over it to even bother. All I have to say for these characters and their ridiculous way of talking is:<br><br><div>
  <br>
  <a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-rUki7znnwws/UeFp67vqtYI/AAAAAAAAEr4/ZvxqM2ewt6g/s1600/regina+shut+up.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img height="172" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380347303ra/701653.gif" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</div><br><br><br><b>Cringe-worthy, horrible writing. </b><br><br>Want some examples?<br><br><i>"Dead bodies started popping up like daisies."</i> p.37<br><br>Really, Bree. Like daisies? This is the best word you could think of to compare the appearance of corpses with?<br><br><i>"My frustration fired like a pottery kiln.</i>" p. 46<br><br>Because Grace is so OMG totally into art, obviously her frustration fires up like a pottery kiln. DUH.<br><br><i>"My head felt like I'd been standing over an open bottle of oil solvent too long."</i> p.70<br><br>Yeah, you probably shouldn't be standing over open bottles of oil solvent. No bueno. However, this does help to explain why Grace is so brain-dead. And maybe also how this book came into being.<br><br>And let's not forget, the ending "action" scenes that were composed of 738 short, choppy sentences that were thrown together and damn-near impossible to follow, and went on for about five pages-- I skimmed through most of what was supposed to be the "climax" of the story because it was beyond boring. Total. Fail.<br><br><b>
  <br>
</b> <b>Treating your readers like sheltered and brain-dead idiots (WARNING: Some profanity ahead, proceed with caution...)</b><br><br>Question: Why is it totally OK to talk about "ripping out throats" in highly graphic/violent terms in YA books but when it comes to swearing or anything sexual we need to talk in secret code?<br><br>Because that's what this book does and it pisses me off to no end. What makes it fine and dandy to write about gory murder and mutilation, but sex and swearing are taboo? Do you really think that teens can't handle reading a few choice swear words? Do you think that mentioning sex or your main character- <i>heaven forbid!</i>-- having sexual thoughts is positively sinful?? THEN DON'T EVEN WRITE IT INTO YOUR BOOK.<br><br>But no- Bree takes the very creative cop-out of having her characters swear and have sexual thoughts, without ever having to actually say specifically what's going on. Because, you know, us readers might just have a brain aneurysm if perfect little Grace hears a swear. So the author chickens out with lines like this:<br><br><i>"The other guy said something vile that I will </i><u>not</u><i> repeat, and then he made an even more disgusting gesture. Daniel told him to go do something to himself and then took my arm and led me to the door." </i>p.67<br><br>I'm sorry.<i> What??</i> So... some guy just said something and made some gesture and then Daniel said something about doing something to himself-- for the love of God, JUST TELL US WHAT YOUR CHARACTERS ARE SAYING! Daniel told the other guy to <i>go fuck himself?</i> Is that what you're trying to say?? Then <u>SAY IT!</u> We aren't going to shatter into a million pieces, Bree, I promise! If you really think your readers are so immature, delicate and sheltered that they can't handle the occasional cuss-word then DON'T even bother implying that your characters swear, because skirting around every "dirty" thing that's being said not only sounds<i> absolutely ridiculous</i>, but it comes across as though you think your readers are total imbeciles. Also, having your main character emphatically refuse to tell me the reader what was just said makes her sound like a stuck-up, self-righteous little toe-rag. ALSO, Daniel grabbing Grace by the arm and dragging her out the door? Yeah, the ENTIRE story reads like Grace is Daniel's pretty piece of property to shove around however he wants. So seriously Ms. Despaine, congratulations on achieving<i> that</i> much epic fail in the span of two sentences. Well-fucking-DONE.<br><br><br><b>Abusive relationship being passed off as romantic</b><br><br>You really don't want to get me effing started with this. <br><br>OK, I'm getting started, since I'm already revved up from my last rant.<br><br>You want to know what's not alright with me? Writing lines like THIS into a book being targeted at young women:<br><br>*****<br><br><i>"Daniel had a way about him that could shut me down in an instant."</i> p. 41<br><br><i>"How did he always do that-- make me completely forget I was mad at him so easily?"</i> p.43<br><br>*****<br><br>Let me be very clear here: This way of thinking is <u>dangerous shit</u>. This is NOT an OK way for girls to think about guys who are emotionally and possibly physically abusive, and no I don't give a rat's patoot that it's only in a fictional book and it's "just a story," so don't even try that with me. This "relationship" between Grace and Daniel is beyond effed up. GOT THAT, Bree?? This is <i>NOT. OK</i>. Portraying women who are so desperately and pathetically controlled by men that they are totally powerless to stop their bullying, threats and domination, and just bend over and take it because they can't help it-- NO, that is effing CRAP! This main character you've created is not a heroine, she's a helpless victim-- and Daniel is <i>not</i> a sexy love interest, he's a disgusting representation of misogyny and violence towards women. The fact that you are passing these kinds of characters off to teen girls as being someone worth emulating or fawning over is highly,<i> highly</i> disturbing. Because yes-- if you look on Goodreads, you'll see young girls saying how "hot" Daniel is-- this chauvinist pig who repeatedly humiliates and chastises the female protag, who can only sit there pathetically worshiping the ground he walks on.<br><br>But it gets even better-- because after Daniel's horrible behavior towards Grace, Grace then comes up with the fantastic idea-- wait for it-- that it's<i> her duty and responsibility to save him</i>. Like, she is actually<i> convicted</i> by this belief that it's her mission to save Daniel who, up to this point, has treated her like pool scum. OMG, someone take this book away from me before I light it on fire. This is seriously some of the most messed up crap I've ever read about in a YA book. <i>Please</i> explain to me again why men are constantly being glorified in YA "literature" as predators and being passed off as romantic and sexy because they treat women like less than poop and could potentially kill them? And then it's up to the female to save them from being assholes? Girls, if you are reading this review, PLEASE realize that guys like this, in books <i>or</i> real life, are NOT hot/sexy/attractive! This is NOT how <i>anyone</i> should be treated! Furthermore, it is absolutely NOT your responsibility to try and turn a "bad guy" around, which is exactly what Grace thinks she should be doing with this crazy, abusive psycho.<br><br>OMGMYHEADISABOUTTOEXPLODE.<br><br><b>Final Thoughts</b><br><br>About three-quarters of the way through <i>The Dark Divine</i>, Grace and Daniel did start to become *marginally* more tolerable. The story *ever-so-slightly* did become more interesting. But unfortunately, by this point the book had been completely ruined by the obnoxious and crappy behavior of the main characters, the dangerous messages about abusive relationships, and the insufferable religious overtones that came across as a blatant moral agenda. So altogether, this just wasn't for me. You might end up loving it as many other readers have, but I just can't recommend it. <br><br>Pretty much, in a nutshell, <i>it blew.</i><br><br><br><br><div>
  <br>
  <a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-OBbSOVba6ss/UeFp_iWP_sI/AAAAAAAAEsA/bxxE-R3JJ6A/s1600/none+for+gretchen+weiners.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img height="162" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380347303ra/701654.gif" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

<div id="review_145393424" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/145393424" />
    <a title="The Rusty Key" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4464559-the-rusty-key"><img alt="The Rusty Key" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1288102499p2/4464559.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/145393424?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="The Rusty Key" class="user" itemprop="url" name="The Rusty Key" href="/user/show/4464559-the-rusty-key">The Rusty Key</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8454770-the-dark-divine">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer145393424" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12110584263239529036">Reviewed by Jordan B. Nielsen<br/><br/><br/>In lieu of a traditional review of The Dark Devine by Bree Despain, I thought we’d play a little game called ‘Paranormal Teen Romance Mad Libs’. <br/><br/>Our story features a girl named (character name, usually containing a common noun and/or adjective). She’s just your typical world weary teen, living in (misty, woodsy, dreary weather locale), an hour outside of (major metro-area) . She isn’t one of the pretty, popular girls, she’s more on the (synonym for plain) and (synony</span>
  <span id="freeText12110584263239529036" style="display:none">Reviewed by Jordan B. Nielsen<br /><br /><br />In lieu of a traditional review of The Dark Devine by Bree Despain, I thought we’d play a little game called ‘Paranormal Teen Romance Mad Libs’. <br /><br />Our story features a girl named (character name, usually containing a common noun and/or adjective). She’s just your typical world weary teen, living in (misty, woodsy, dreary weather locale), an hour outside of (major metro-area) . She isn’t one of the pretty, popular girls, she’s more on the (synonym for plain) and (synonym for clumsy) side. She has a friend who is kind of a (synonym for air-head). In her free time, she really enjoys (Photography/Drawing/Painting/Reading – circle one). In spite of the fact that she’s (synonym for bland) and (synonym for self righteous) and (synonym for not very pretty) she has (pick a number more than 1) perfectly nice guys who are in love with her, all of whom she distains for no good reason, when really such a (synonym for dullard) should be thrilled that anyone can even separate her from the wallpaper. <br /><br />Then one day a new guy appears. She is immediately drawn to him like a (synonym for prey) to a (synonym for predator). His name is (select a name no one has given a child in the last 200 years). Not only is he (synonym for wildly attractive) he’s also got that (synonym for dark) and (synonym for brooding) thing going on. To prove it, he drives a motorcycle. While most sensible people would think he’s (Charles Manson/Ted Kaczynski/The Zodiac Killer - circle one) our narrator is completely enamored of him, though spends (pick a number more than 1) chapters stubbornly insisting that she hates his gorgeous, gorgeous guts. <br /><br />But there’s more to this (jerk/loser/misanthrope/recluse –circle two) than meets the eye: he has a secret. Through (pick a number morethan 1) chapters our girl doggedly stalks this guy she claims to loathe with her head (pick a place one might shove their head if they were quite stupid). She tediously tries to figure out what the heck is going on, while it’s plainly obvious to the reader by the abundance of (werewolf claws/vampire fangs/angel feathers/unicorn horns - circle one) that keep falling out of the dude’s coat pocket. <br /><br />At the point when he, and we, can’t take her imbecility anymore, this mysterious guy breaks down and overtly explains to the girl that he is a (chose a mythological creature). Rather than question weather or not she was experiencing some sort of psychotic episode upon hearing this information, as anyone else would, she responds by (biting her lip/chewing her nails/playing with her hair – circle one) and is generally (synonym for nonplused) by this improbable revelation. <br /><br />Now in the honeymoon phase of their new relationship, the two take to nature and (fly/run really fast/jump really high – circle one) through some trees, saying things like “You have no idea how amazing you are.” Neither do we. Mercifully, this gooey romp will eventually be disrupted by the symptoms of our romantic hero’s paranormal affliction, resulting in (shaking/sweating/clenching fists/clenching gorgeous square jaw/howling – pick two). So consumed is our main character by her nauseating new relationship, that she’ll accidentally blow off her (friend/family member –circle one)’s really super important (birthday/sleepover/wedding/child birth/graduation/holiday celebration/funeral/wake – circle one) which she totally promised she would go to. But it’s ok, because all side characters in this book are purely ornamental and seldom even given names. And you shouldn’t even consider thinking of her as a completely (synonym for selfish) (word that rhymes with witch), she’s just in love and you would like, totally do the same thing if it were you.<br /><br />But of course, in all this (synonym for obsessive) time they’re spending together, our young lovers won’t be consummating their towering inferno of feelings because (he’ll accidentally kill her in the process/this book is completely unrealistic/this book is full of sexist, puritanical overtones/parents will freak out and refuse to buy it for their teens, thus hurting sales – circle two). But really the thought of these two getting intimate is thoroughly (synonym for icky) anyways, as they have about as much chemistry as a wet mop and a potato.<br /><br />Oh yeah. And there is some sort of trouble involving a (pick a scary monster), which, after a lot of (synonym for hand wringing) and (consulting old books/googling – pick one) will be wrapped up easily because of our guy’s (super human strength/ability to fly/general invincibility/insistence by the publishers that he not die in the first book because they want to milk a franchise out of this – circle one). <br /><br />Did you get it filled out? Congratulations, you are now a writer. Go get yourself an agent because you’re going to sell a LOT of books. If you’re into this sort of story, The Dark Devine will be right up your alley. If you feel you got enough of it out of the 1000+ pages of the Twilight Saga, I suggest you move along. <br /><br /><br /><br />For more reviews from The Rusty Key, visit us at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.therustykey.com">www.therustykey.com</a></span>

<div id="review_58844471" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/58844471" />
    <a title="Jess (The Cozy Reader) Kennedy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2139555-jess-the-cozy-reader-kennedy"><img alt="Jess (The Cozy Reader) Kennedy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1272737111p2/2139555.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/58844471?book_show_action=true">Jun 08, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jess (The Cozy Reader) Kennedy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jess (The Cozy Reader) Kennedy" href="/user/show/2139555-jess-the-cozy-reader-kennedy">Jess (The Cozy Reader) Kennedy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">young adult, fantasy, paranormal</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2139555-jess-the-cozy-reader-kennedy?shelf=author-signed">author-signed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2139555-jess-the-cozy-reader-kennedy?shelf=contest-prize">contest-prize</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2139555-jess-the-cozy-reader-kennedy?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2139555-jess-the-cozy-reader-kennedy?shelf=keeper">keeper</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer58844471" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11695936959164060564">My Grade<br/><br/>Plot: 5<br/>Setting: 4<br/>Writing: 5<br/>Originality: 5<br/>Characters: 5<br/>Passion: 5<br/>Overall: 29/30 = 96% =A<br/>Cover/Title Bonus: 4<br/><br/><br/>I won this ARC on Bree’s blog in one of her monthly pre-release celebrations for The Dark Divine. I also got a bottle of matching nail polish as seen on the cover and a pedicure kit! :)<br/><br/><br/>Summary (Bree’s website)<br/><br/> A prodigal son<br/> A dangerous love<br/> A deadly secret . . .<br/> I stood back and watched his movements. Daniel had that way about him that could shut me down in an instant. . . . I kick</span>
  <span id="freeText11695936959164060564" style="display:none">My Grade<br /><br />Plot: 5<br />Setting: 4<br />Writing: 5<br />Originality: 5<br />Characters: 5<br />Passion: 5<br />Overall: 29/30 = 96% =A<br />Cover/Title Bonus: 4<br /><br /><br />I won this ARC on Bree’s blog in one of her monthly pre-release celebrations for The Dark Divine. I also got a bottle of matching nail polish as seen on the cover and a pedicure kit! :)<br /><br /><br />Summary (Bree’s website)<br /><br /> A prodigal son<br /> A dangerous love<br /> A deadly secret . . .<br /> I stood back and watched his movements. Daniel had that way about him that could shut me down in an instant. . . . I kicked the gravel a couple of times and worked up my courage again. “Tell me . . . I mean . . . why did you come back? Why now, after all this time?”<br /> Grace Divine, daughter of the local pastor, always knew something terrible happened the night Daniel Kalbi disappeared—the night she found her brother Jude collapsed on the porch, covered in blood. But she has no idea what a truly monstrous secret that night really held. And when Daniel returns three years later, Grace can no longer deny her attraction to him, despite promising Jude she’ll stay away.<br /> As Grace gets closer to Daniel, her actions stir the ancient evil Daniel unleashed that horrific night. Grace must discover the truth behind Jude and Daniel's dark secret . . . and the cure that can save the ones she loves. But she may have to lay down the ultimate sacrifice to do it—her soul.<br /><br /><br />Excerpt (Bree’s Website)<br />The first chapter is available to read on Bree’s website. It’s very good!<br /><br /><br />Plot<br /><br />The above summary does an amazing job at explaining what’s going on without saying too much. This book is written so well it all flows amazingly well and keeps you guessing what will happen next.<br /><br />There’s a major artist theme going on in here too. Both Grace and Daniel draw/paint, him better than her, and it’s a very cool common bond they share.<br /><br />The ending was handled wonderfully. I enjoyed this entire book.<br /><br /><br /><br />Setting<br /><br />The town is said to be near Apple Valley. A lot happens in the art class, the parish, the Divine house and backyard and downtown.<br /><br />It’s a fairly common setting with nothing really standing out.<br /><br />I particularly enjoyed the tree climbing and finding baby James the best. OH! And the angel memorial: awesome.<br /><br />It’s present time.<br /><br />Writing<br /><br />Amazing. Seriously. I can’t explain how it’s written but it’s written very well. It’s not like books I’ve read recently. The tone is unique in a way that makes me second guess myself each page turn. The details that you’ll be guessing at are within reach but you don’t reach them until the exact moment that Grace does. LOVE THAT! I hate figuring it out before the main character. I had my guesses but so did Grace but neither of us knew until it was there.<br /><br />It’s written in Grace’s POV the entire time. I wished I could get into Daniel’s head a time or three. He was very interesting and I wanted to know more about him.<br /><br />Originality<br /><br />I knew what Daniel was when I read the first chapter on Bree’s website. But like I explained above Bree had me second guessing myself the entire book. So, even though I’d figured it out already I just didn’t feel 100% confident that I really knew and that kept my interest at top notch. I honestly couldn’t put the book down! I finished it at 2:00 am!<br /><br />What Daniel is is easy to figure out but it gets explained very well. I enjoyed the details and thought they were very original.<br /><br /><br /><br />Characters<br /><br />Grace is the main character. She’s the daughter of the Pastor. “Pastor D-vine.” :) She’s still struggling with Daniel’s disappearance from a few years prior and doesn’t handle his return very well. She’s clearly head over heels for him and it makes her sad, angry, and heart broken.<br /><br />Jude is Grace’s older brother. He’s a sweet guy, always helping others, but he’s troubled by the attack from Daniel a few years prior. He doesn’t like or trust Daniel.<br /><br />Grace’s Dad is cool. He’s all about helping others too. He nearly goes mad trying to help Daniel and ultimately his entire family it seems. I enjoyed his character a lot.<br /><br />Daniel. Daniel is the black sheep of his family. They abandoned him a few years back. His mom choose his dad over him, only a young boy. He returns to his home town looking for a fresh start.<br /><br /><br />Passion<br /><br />This is my favorite category but sometimes it’s the hardest to review. There are major sparks flying between Daniel and Grace. I love that it was there in the story but it wasn’t the front runner. Their relationship plays a huge role in the book yet it was handled with great care. I enjoyed their relationship immensely. Me? Beat around the bush? No…..<br /><br /><br />Overall<br /><br />Amazing. Awesome. Superb. An unexpected thrill of a ride. I knew it was going to be good but it surpassed my expectations. It was written so well. Everything was covered and it ended well wrapped up.<br /><br /><br />Cover/Title Bonus<br /><br />The title is awesome. The cover….it’s beautiful and catches the eye but it doesn’t represent the book very well. I’m not sure if I’m missing something or what but I’m not crazy about the cover after reading the book. It’s gorgeous but it lacks focus or direct representation of the story. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11695936959164060564" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_98475602" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/98475602" />
    <a title="Annalisa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/542037-annalisa"><img alt="Annalisa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1226336540p2/542037.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/98475602?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annalisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annalisa" href="/user/show/542037-annalisa">Annalisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">paranormal romance fans</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Annalisa by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/947145-janessa">Janessa</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/542037-annalisa?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/542037-annalisa?shelf=cover">cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/542037-annalisa?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/542037-annalisa?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer98475602" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12171269697479079892">Good girl, studious protagonist: check<br/>Dark, mysterious boy who is really the good guy but starts off being incredibly cruel: check<br/>Unexplained sexual tension that controls protagonist: check<br/>Perfect guy who isn't perfect: check<br/>Love triangle: check<br/>Best friend who gets protagonist to do something dangerous: check<br/>Contrived plot elements to keep the reader in suspense: check<br/><br/>I don't know why I keep reading these when this post-Twilight formula for fantasy romances doesn't work for me. Having said that,</span>
  <span id="freeText12171269697479079892" style="display:none">Good girl, studious protagonist: check<br />Dark, mysterious boy who is really the good guy but starts off being incredibly cruel: check<br />Unexplained sexual tension that controls protagonist: check<br />Perfect guy who isn't perfect: check<br />Love triangle: check<br />Best friend who gets protagonist to do something dangerous: check<br />Contrived plot elements to keep the reader in suspense: check<br /><br />I don't know why I keep reading these when this post-Twilight formula for fantasy romances doesn't work for me. Having said that, Despain manages to explain her fantasy elements and give good foreshadowing clues, Grace's family is actually involved in her life (although I found her pastor family a little too tainted by Mormon family), I liked Grace and Daniel some of the time (him more than her), and the end surprised me. I don't why. It was obvious, but I wasn't too invested in the story at that point to think about it (not the secret but the twist at the end). <br /><br />The second half of the book kind of fell apart until the climax. I had been anxious for answers in the beginning, but then Despian stretched out Grace's indecision without fleshing out her internal struggle just so she could space out vital information and race to the climax. I wanted to know why Grace wasn't reading the letters I think she would have devoured. I wanted to know what was going on with Jude when Grace gave up seeing Daniel for him. I wanted to know more about her father's plans and beliefs. And I wanted to know more about Daniel and what it was he wanted to tell her. The climax was good, and I like said surprised me, but I wanted more going into it.<br /><br />I'm not sure what to rate it. It wasn't my thing, but I can see girls who like paranormal romance really liking it and it's just as good and bad as everything else in the genre. For that, I'm rating 2.5 stars. Just not my thing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12171269697479079892" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1426024347" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1426024347" />
    <a title="LilyCat (Agent of SHIELD)-- on hiatus :(" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44797462-lilycat-agent-of-shield----on-hiatus"><img alt="LilyCat (Agent of SHIELD)-- on hiatus :(" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1462503379p2/44797462.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1426024347?book_show_action=true">Oct 26, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="LilyCat (Agent of SHIELD)-- on hiatus :(" class="user" itemprop="url" name="LilyCat (Agent of SHIELD)-- on hiatus :(" href="/user/show/44797462-lilycat-agent-of-shield----on-hiatus">LilyCat (Agent of SHIELD)-- on hiatus :(</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44797462-lilycat-agent-of-shield----on-hiatus?shelf=pretty-cover">pretty-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44797462-lilycat-agent-of-shield----on-hiatus?shelf=modern-setting">modern-setting</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44797462-lilycat-agent-of-shield----on-hiatus?shelf=cliche-alert">cliche-alert</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44797462-lilycat-agent-of-shield----on-hiatus?shelf=boring">boring</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44797462-lilycat-agent-of-shield----on-hiatus?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44797462-lilycat-agent-of-shield----on-hiatus?shelf=woe-is-me-mc">woe-is-me-mc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44797462-lilycat-agent-of-shield----on-hiatus?shelf=stalker-boyfriend">stalker-boyfriend</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44797462-lilycat-agent-of-shield----on-hiatus?shelf=pretty-dress-cover">pretty-dress-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44797462-lilycat-agent-of-shield----on-hiatus?shelf=good-cover-bad-book">good-cover-bad-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44797462-lilycat-agent-of-shield----on-hiatus?shelf=useless-heroine">useless-heroine</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1426024347" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10215110123075704355">Sorry guys for totally forgetting to review this whole list of books... I've been a bit busy with school.<br/><br/><b>The Gist:</b> Good girl Grace Divine (*cringes at name*), daughter of the local pastor, has a run-in with her childhood friend Daniel, now a mysterious bad boy, whom she hasn't seen in years since he disappeared- and left her brother in a pool of blood. Grace's brother, Jude, acts openly hostile towards Daniel and tells her his suspicions, but also starts behaving erratically. As Grace and Daniel</span>
  <span id="freeText10215110123075704355" style="display:none">Sorry guys for totally forgetting to review this whole list of books... I've been a bit busy with school.<br><br><b>The Gist:</b> Good girl Grace Divine (*cringes at name*), daughter of the local pastor, has a run-in with her childhood friend Daniel, now a mysterious bad boy, whom she hasn't seen in years since he disappeared- and left her brother in a pool of blood. Grace's brother, Jude, acts openly hostile towards Daniel and tells her his suspicions, but also starts behaving erratically. As Grace and Daniel fall in love, she discovers what he'd been trying to hide-- he comes from a line of wolf shapeshifters who are prone to temptation and corruption from their powers. When gory murders are discovered in her town, Grace wants to suspect Daniel, but she has a feeling it's someone else, and they're after both her and Daniel.<br><br>Genre: Fantasy (paranormal, werewolves, urban fantasy)<br>Maturity: moderate romance, some disturbing violence, some crude language (11+)<br><br><b>New Review</b><br>I started worrying when my edition had a Becca Fitzpatrick endorsement on the back.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1469832210i/19863228.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>No wonder Fitzpatrick endorsed this book! About 25% in, I realized it was basically her own novel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6339664.Hush__Hush__Hush__Hush___1_" title="Hush, Hush (Hush, Hush, #1) by Becca Fitzpatrick" rel="nofollow noopener"> Hush Hush</a>, except with werewolves instead of angels. Brainless Mary Sue meets a hot jerk "bad boy" who seduces her while all the while I am throwing up <b>red flags for potential sexual harassment and stalking behavior</b>, all told in a boring, mind-shredding narrative with a few grating side characters like a "best friend" and a cheesy villain thrown in at the end that anyone could have seen from <b>a mile away.</b> (Wow that was a long sentence.)<br><br>The plot revolves around a lot of contrived mystery about weird murders and events in the town, when <b>the author basically THROWS werewolf hints at us</b>, mostly word choice clues that are SUPER awkward, ex. so and so "yips" or "barks." (BTW, to combat the "dog" references, I have added Grumpy Cat memes throughout.) After some religious filler from Grace's dad, a pastor, there's a lot of creepy romance, then a bunch of "action" that is basically Daniel saving Grace. Everything else is emotionless filler, making this relatively short book a chore to slog through.<br><br>The bad boy + good girl dynamic seemed totally cliche to me, and included a lot of over-the-top corny lines that I kept cringing at. Grace angsts constantly about how some family drama makes him "forbidden" to her. It's a really long, stupid story I don't really want to talk about. <b>But of course, we all know to YA heroines, like small children, making something off-limits makes it suddenly cool.</b> (This trope AGAIN.)<br><br>The "bad boy good girl" romance also, apparently, means to the author that Grace is "conflicted"-- that is, talks in that very dangerous YA doublespeak. "Giving into sexy temptation" for Grace means protesting weakly when all along, she wants to do it.<br><blockquote>
<i>[Daniel] shifted forward on the seat of his bike. "You coming?"<br>"What? No, I can't." [...] [I] climbed onto the back of his motorcycle.</i> (p. 104)</blockquote><br>This is the whole "no means yes" crap we get all the time in YA. It's annoying-- girl, make up your mind! and also dangerous, because <b>it tells guys that even if a girl clearly says she is uncomfortable with doing something, she secretly wants to do it, and it is actually permission. It tells girls to not speak their minds.</b> Here are some common examples of this kind of doublespeak:<br><blockquote>
<br>"I hate you"= "I actually love you"<br>"No, stop!!" = "Yes, please!"<br>"Go away!"= "come hither, handsome hunk."<br>"Don't touch me!" = "I'm playing hard-to-get."<br>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1469832210i/19863229.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Characters...<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1466280593i/19462448.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Grace's whole gig is "squeaky clean Puritan." Like, she is a legit freaking Puritan from the days of the Mayflower- ankle-length skirts, abhors swearing, even quotes the Bible in KJV with all the "thees" and "thous." She hates swearing so much even her narration is cleaned up in a really awkward way.<br><blockquote>
<i><br>[Pete] called her <b>something quite unfavorable</b> under his breath.</i> (320)<br><br><i>Daniel told him to <b>go do something to himself.</b></i>
</blockquote><br>Like, I get that Grace doesn't want to swear, but her not wanting to even <i>think</i> about swearing by relaying it in her narration is really annoying and obstructs the story and emotions of the other characters. (Well, it's not as bad as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9284655.Tiger_s_Curse__The_Tiger_Saga___1_" title="Tiger's Curse (The Tiger Saga, #1) by Colleen Houck" rel="nofollow noopener"> Tiger's Curse</a>, where the MC "angrily" calls a guy a "wily scoundrel." So there's that.)<br><br><b>Grace is the classic hyperinsecure girl who is ACTUALLY 100% perfect, she's just too dumb to see everyone worshiping her all the time.</b> She's pretty, (supposedly) smart and good at art, etc. etc. To make things worse, the cutest, smartest, most athletic senior on campus, Pete, is madly in love with her, but as I predicted, she stomps over his niceness to run straight to emo jerk Daniel, who doesn't even treat her like a person for about half the book (until he takes a heel face turn and becomes a suddenly sweet loving model boyfriend). She's also pretty mean to her friend, April, by constantly comparing her to a dog. It's annoying because not only is she being mean, it's also part of the whole "dropping dog/werewolf hints every 5 seconds" thing that Bree Despain does.<br><blockquote>
<i><br>April was </i>so<i> like my old dog Daisy in that way.<br><br>April's voice had a high, doglike whine to it.</i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1466280593i/19462449._SX540_.jpg" width="467" height="329" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The way Grace compares April to a dog suggests April is dumb, blindly loyal, annoying, and clingy, and also suggests that Grace is inconsiderate and treats her so-called "best friend" like crap.<br><br>Despite Grace saying April's pretty dumb, she herself isn't exactly a genius herself. For example, let's see how Grace treats <b>medieval historical documents on loan from a foreign country</b>.<br><blockquote>
  <i><br>I carefully turned to the last letter I'd read. Half of it was missing- disintegrated in the hostile environment of my school bag.</i>
</blockquote><br>These are priceless, centuries-old letters from the Crusades that her dad is borrowing from a freaking MUSEUM, yet Grace just casually tosses them into the bottom of her bag like they're old homework papers.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1466283002i/19462695._SX540_.jpg" width="450" height="360" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Other examples of her lack of logic circuits- when her brother Jude says Daniel is dangerous, Grace instinctively responds Jude has to be wrong for the sole reason that <i>she's in love with Daniel, THEREFORE Daniel can't be evil.</i> That's as far as her reasoning goes.<br><blockquote>
  <i>The things [Jude] said couldn't be anything but lies. <b>How could I feel the way I did about Daniel otherwise?</b></i>
  <br>
  <br>
  <i>I gazed into Daniel's eyes. They were deep and soft and familiar. My brother had to be lying.</i>
</blockquote><br>Yes, you saw that logic gap. Grace goes straight from gazing into Daniel's eyes to concluding Jude is wrong. Unfortunately, dreamy eye-staring isn't exactly a polygraph, no matter what stupid YA characters think.<br><br>And as if to add insult to injury, all the while, she is spouting "strong female lines," such as when, on page 196, she says, <i>"I'm not stupid or fragile or weak, you know."</i> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1466283002i/19462696.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>You tell 'em, Grumpy Cat!!<br><br>Daniel isn't much better. He antagonizes Grace constantly, proving 1) he's a jerk, and 2) they're gonna fall in love.<br><blockquote>
  <i>I felt something plink against my head. "Hey, Grace," Daniel stage-whispered.<br><br>"Kiss me and I'll give it back."</i>
</blockquote><br>To make things worse, Daniel does stupid and creepy crap all the time to be a "sexy sinner," ex. jumping over a fence to hang out with Grace in a GRAVEYARD and telling Grace she has to kiss him for him to give her stuff back (ew). (Need I say I'd rather kiss a pile of steaming werewolf crap than this guy.) OR <i>jumping into Grace's bedroom uninvited... while she's in a bathrobe.</i> Then, he makes a huge flip and suddenly, he's a sweet model boyfriend who is really damaged and tortured.<br><blockquote>
  <i> "What I am... it's why no one can ever love me."</i>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1466283002i/19462697.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1466283002i/19462698.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Jude, Grace's brother, opposes Grace and Daniel's relationship, so OF COURSE he turns out to be cray-cray. Anyone can see that from a mile away. He starts out as a jerk, then turns into a paranoid, crazy jerk. It's plainly obvious that something's wrong with him, but no one seems to notice.<br><br>Pete is the character I really felt bad for. He starts out as a nice guy, but then, to crush all hopes of an alternate ship, the author just ALSO gives him a heel face turn and he becomes a cold unfeeling jerk and then a freaking psycho. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[He acts super out of character and even tries to RAPE Grace at the end of the book, probably just to highlight how "saintly" Daniel is. Of course, between a plain jerk and a freaking RAPIST, it's no contest, but if you really need to have a RAPIST to show that Daniel is a good person, it's honestly kind of sad. Also, rape is NOT a plot device to be used lightly, which Despain does-- there's no follow up. Grace is like, "hey my ex just tried to rape me, I'm fine, it's all cool."<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1469832210i/19863230._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>Conclusion:</b> A very dull, cliche book with its share of Twilight tropes and a jerk love interest.<br><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="10215110123075704355" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_98832688" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/98832688" />
    <a title="Amelia, free market Puritan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan"><img alt="Amelia, free market Puritan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508223427p2/1852293.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/98832688?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amelia, free market Puritan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amelia, free market Puritan" href="/user/show/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan">Amelia, free market Puritan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan?shelf=ya-kids-teen">ya-kids-teen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan?shelf=loveable-love-story">loveable-love-story</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan?shelf=arcs">arcs</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer98832688" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2408993180803080490">I LOVED THIS BOOK!<br/>Simply put, <i>The Dark Divine</i> exceeded all my expectations. Paranormal, bad boy and ordinary girl - who hasn't seen that before? Well, the relationship in this story was very well-done and evenly paced, and the "paranormal" aspect was so incredibly original and entertaining, so it felt like I was reading something completely fresh and new. Bree Despain's take on werewolves - which I'm sure we're all familiar with - is so INCREDIBLY original and actually makes sense! I remember th</span>
  <span id="freeText2408993180803080490" style="display:none">I LOVED THIS BOOK!<br />Simply put, <i>The Dark Divine</i> exceeded all my expectations. Paranormal, bad boy and ordinary girl - who hasn't seen that before? Well, the relationship in this story was very well-done and evenly paced, and the "paranormal" aspect was so incredibly original and entertaining, so it felt like I was reading something completely fresh and new. Bree Despain's take on werewolves - which I'm sure we're all familiar with - is so INCREDIBLY original and actually makes sense! I remember thinking, "yeah, definitely! Why not?" Bravo, Mrs. Despain!<br />I especially liked the inclusion of useful, responsible parent-figures. I think we can all agree that parent figures in YA are frequently absent, so it was nice to have helpful parent characters. Now, I do think that sometimes the Divine family was portrayed a little on the stereotypical side: Grace and Jude are great characters, and I DO know boys like Jude, so no, I don't believe that he's "unrealistic" at all - but sometimes they acted a little too contrived (my cousins are children of a pastor, and they do NOT spend their free time at food pantries, nor do they discuss clothing drives. Maybe they *should*, but...) But that one little mention is the only thing that I can think of to say about this book: aside from the Divine family's kind-of blatant portrayal, all the characters were very real, very well-rounded, and easy to relate to. It's always a plus to have grounded, practical characters with values and a good head on their shoulders. Now Grace isn't perfect, but she is a genuinely caring person, and that made up for any lapses in judgment throughout the story. Jude is a really interesting character, too. At the beginning, he was a little too Richie Cunningham for me, but as the Prodigal Son scenario played out, both he and Daniel became incredibly fun to explore.<br />Daniel and Grace's relationship was very well-done. It wasn't rushed, but it didn't beat around the bush; it wasn't abusive, it wasn't superficial, it wasn't inappropriate. Rather, I found Grace's devotion to Daniel and her (ultimate) willingness to help him very touching.<br />Even though this <s>book</s> series really doesn't have a designated villain (yet), the plot remained strong and interesting throughout, and the story was evenly paced. <i>The Dark Divine</i> was a fast read, but that's mainly because I was so engrossed, I could not put it down!<br /><br />I really can't praise this book enough. Yes, there are religious elements in this story, but I suppose I missed the memo that decided that was a bad thing. :P Kidding aide, I hope that doesn't dissuade anyone from picking up <i>TDD</i>. It is a well-written, captivating, and incredibly romantic story, and I sincerely recommend it to fantasy/YA lovers!<br />I'd like to say thank-you to Bree for the story she created, and the way in which she decided to tell it. I'm definitely a fan, and I eagerly look forward to her next installment =]</span>
  <a data-text-id="2408993180803080490" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText9992064488273567680" style="display:none">Three words; I. Loved. It!<br /><br />The pages inside are just as full of intrigue and mystery as the beautiful cover itself!<br /><br />Wow! What an awesome debut! Picked this one up, and didn't put it down until I was finished. Not only was there great charactizations, extraordinary writing and a infallible mystery, but the story itself was just spectacular!<br /><br />I loved Despain's talent of weaving ideas of mythology seamlessly into the everyday world. The daily struggle of Grace's life, being the person she wants to be, and being the person that everyone expects her to be as a preacher's daughter, marvelously parallels the life of the everyday teenager.... preacher father or not. <br /><br />The plot was quick and engaging and the ending is completely satisfying, while leaving the possibility for a sequel without being a cliffhanger. <br /><br />This was just a fun book to read. I enjoyed reading about these characters and watching the plot unfold and the mystery ultimately revealed. Like I said before.... awesome debut! <br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2807038172902586370">This is such a cheap rip-off of the Twilight series. I won't even begin to go into all of the similarities; it's not worth my time. Suffice it to say, I was consistently rolling my eyes throughout the entire story. The only difference between this and Twilight is that Despain adds a clear Biblical take. It's sad that that is really the <i>only</i> original part of the whole story. This one has officially made my "no-dice" bookshelf on GR. I am so thankful this was a library book and I didn't spend any </span>
  <span id="freeText2807038172902586370" style="display:none">This is such a cheap rip-off of the Twilight series. I won't even begin to go into all of the similarities; it's not worth my time. Suffice it to say, I was consistently rolling my eyes throughout the entire story. The only difference between this and Twilight is that Despain adds a clear Biblical take. It's sad that that is really the <i>only</i> original part of the whole story. This one has officially made my "no-dice" bookshelf on GR. I am so thankful this was a library book and I didn't spend any money to read it!<br /><br />UPDATE: My friend Nikki asked me about this book in a round-about-way and I think it's worth posting what I told her:<br /><br />[This] is the worst YA book I've ever read! It was such a piece of uncreative trash--all Despain did was take the Twilight story and tweak it so that the 'bad boy' was a ***SPOILER ALERT***hell hound rather than a vamp. There was even a piggy-back ride scene through the woods for crying out loud! (For the record, that also happens in Twilight.) I would rather read a poorly written original story than one with pretty packaging that's a total rip-off. I'm a Christian, but I also got completely fed-up with Despain's overbearing religious slant in the novel (and I've read several Christian novels that were nothing like hers). The main girl's name is Grace Divine and her dad is a preacher and we got to hear over and over and over again about how she needs to live up to her name. Puhlease! The books just drips with it's own self importance.</span>
