    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_85024046" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/85024046" />
    <a title="Heather" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2615211-heather"><img alt="Heather" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1265909675p2/2615211.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/85024046?book_show_action=true">Jan 14, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heather" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heather" href="/user/show/2615211-heather">Heather</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2615211-heather?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer85024046" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7856627147781172512">Despite a really terrible job on the part of her publisher (missing words and typos abound, parsed out in a font so large and overwhelming in its boldness that I was distracted to no end, and enclosed in a bizarre cover that looks more like an erotic novel than a YA horror/paranormal fantasy), I was really, really pleasantly surprised by this story. <br/><br/>MILD SPOILERS:<br/>Grace Divine is the daughter of a pastor in a conservative church-going community, but her straitlaced family has spent the last sever</span>
  <span id="freeText7856627147781172512" style="display:none">Despite a really terrible job on the part of her publisher (missing words and typos abound, parsed out in a font so large and overwhelming in its boldness that I was distracted to no end, and enclosed in a bizarre cover that looks more like an erotic novel than a YA horror/paranormal fantasy), I was really, really pleasantly surprised by this story. <br /><br />MILD SPOILERS:<br />Grace Divine is the daughter of a pastor in a conservative church-going community, but her straitlaced family has spent the last several years hiding and avoiding the fate of their unofficial foster son and brother Daniel, and his strange disappearance. Grace is caught in a sort of accepting malaise of this status quo until Daniel shows up at her high school. While Grace's older brother Jude demands she avoid Daniel, and her parents appear to be avoiding the entire situation, Grace falls back on her old affections for her childhood friend and determines to use her dad's pastoral "care for those in need" motto with Daniel, too. Which, of course, results in all kinds of drama, secrets, blood, death, chaos and kissing, etc.<br /><br />At first glance this looked like another typical mysterious-bad-boy novel that usually makes me cringe -- why do we insist on parading these horrible jerks before young women as model friends and lovers? -- but ho'd on, all is not as it seems. Yes, Daniel has a secret that turns out to be another commonly used plot twist in fantasy these days, and yes, Grace is a little slow on the uptake (the word lycanthrope didn't tip her off). But I'm gonna be honest -- until I saw the word lycanthrope, I wasn't tipped off, either. Despain does a really decent job of holding together the suspense throughout this novel; even after the sort-of big reveal of Daniel's identity, nothing's as clean-cut as you'd expect. If Jude's fate was a little easy to predict, I'll allow it given that I didn't find it so until a good 150 pages in, and that was enough for me. And even if some of the plot, including Grace's name, reminded me of my much-loved copy of Maggie Stiefvater's novel <i>Shiver</i>, <i>The Dark Divine</i> is an entirely different mood. While <i>Shiver</i> moves the story through a solemn, almost hushed internalization, <i>The Dark Divine</i> packs in a fair amount of action and suspense. I think the comparisons I've heard to Stephanie Meyer's <i>New Moon</i> is a little unfair in this regard, as well; in <i>New Moon</i>, Bella doesn't do a whole heck of a lot. In <i>Divine</i>, Grace is so busy trying to do whatever she thinks is the morally right thing -- respect her parents, listen to her brother, help Daniel, put up with the local charity case -- that she's completely wrapped up in the darker deeds around her (because c'mon, no church-going gal should be THAT laid back about the kind of party she walked into at Daniel's) until her deductions hit her on the head like a proverbial ton'o'bricks.<br /><br />But here are the biggest ways that <i>The Dark Divine</i> is unlike any of its similar sister novels -- Grace is a church kid, and darn it, she's cool with that. Some readers may be turned off by the strong and frequent references to Judeo-Christian values and kitsch (right down to printed church bulletins), and oppositely, those in the religous environmental know may find her one-dimensional harpy of a mother a little hard to stomach, but you gotta give it to Despain, she talks about Grace's Protestant bubble without batting an eye. Grace goes to Bible study; volunteers for her dad's church charities; asks Daniel not to swear in the halls of her Christian school; and ponders the real implications of the Prodigal Son. She's sheltered; she wouldn't know what Buffy the Vampire Slayer or Gaiman's Sandman would look like if they bit her, so every monstrous revelation is doubly new and shocking to her. <br /><br />It may not be cool, or even likeable to some, but Grace's religious viewpoints do make her a real standout in this genre. Sometimes it's just the facts; with her Dad a pastor, it's inevitable she'll be describing a way of life (no web surfing in her room; spaghetti straps are verboten) that many cannot relate to. But she's still relatable, if for no other reason than those honest moments when she's thinking in the paradigm of her religious views, and most protagonists in YA fiction are trying to figure out some sort of paradigm, too. Grace asks herself, if Daniel's the prodigal and Jude's the "good son," then doesn't the parable infer the good son is the one in the most danger? What does "honor thy father and mother" really mean when said parents are keeping secrets that have hurt people? When another father and mother in the story subject their child to terrifying abuse and abandonment? How do children recover from that kind of abuse? And how do their comfy teenage friends figure out how to help them in a way that's truly meaningful? Just how far should grace and forgiveness go, when there's family at stake and blood on someone's hands?<br /><br />And consequently, Daniel's a little raw. Despain's publishers may want to convince us he's a bad boy, but really, he's a good boy subjected to so much abuse and heartache that he's done some pretty bad stuff to try to cope. In a novel ripe with Grace's naivete, Daniel doesn't waste any words about the many hedonistic forms his self-hatred and escape have taken. He's a social misfit and a castout when Grace first sees him, and despite a clean-up in his general appearance, that never really changes. Everyone, and I mean EVERYONE, rejects him in the most heartbreaking ways. Heartbreaking, for me, because in the midst of a paranormal story, these accounts of rejection and neglect are palpably realistic. Somewhere along the way, Despain got a solid grasp on the pain and injustices teenagers suffer at the hands of the very family and adults who are supposed to protect them. Her insistence in defining acts of grace bump up against these gritty realities and keep the novel's voice unique, thoughtful, and relevant. Despain's telling us that you don't have to make your characters angry, bitter, cussing Goth kids to tell a story about pain, and redemption, that teenagers and adults can relate to. It's old fashioned but not cloying -- religious, yes, but not preachy, and because these elements were so surprising, I enjoyed the plot surprises, too. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7856627147781172512" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4175738394381935734">The Dark Divine is truly an amazing book! It captured my heart from page one, and took me on an amazing ride of suspense, mystery, conviction, and unconditional love. <br/><br/>Bree Despain took a traditional stance with werewolves, but added a twist.   <span id="freeText4175738394381935734" style="display:none">The Dark Divine is truly an amazing book! It captured my heart from page one, and took me on an amazing ride of suspense, mystery, conviction, and unconditional love. <br /><br />Bree Despain took a traditional stance with werewolves, but added a twist. These are not mere shape shifters like current novels would portray, but more like the fairytale monsters we imagined them to be as children. I appreciated the amount of back history she put into their origin of the Urbat. The contrast their original nature as Heaven's Hounds, to their later downfall, Hounds of death. <br /><br />The Divine family is one that I totally related with! The character's of this family were developed so well, they are believable. My heart broke for our prodigal ... Daniel, with his tragic childhood. It only made his redemptive story all the more endearing. I had a box of tissues next to my chair and used them often! :) <br /><br />Honestly, I would implore you to pick up a copy of this book and read it now instead of reading this review. It is everything it promises to be and so much more. <br /><br />Artistically beautiful, The Dark Divine is a story with redemptive qualities where true love conquers all!<br /><br /><br />Now it's time to go hunt for Jude in "The Lost Saint"!</span>

<div id="review_147403075" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/147403075" />
    <a title="Nhi Le (The Literary Bystander)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3525540-nhi-le-the-literary-bystander"><img alt="Nhi Le (The Literary Bystander)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1395462441p2/3525540.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/147403075?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nhi Le (The Literary Bystander)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nhi Le (The Literary Bystander)" href="/user/show/3525540-nhi-le-the-literary-bystander">Nhi Le (The Literary Bystander)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer147403075" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4517882892840160594"><b>In a Nuthsell:</b> You may be asking: alright, so I've got a fairly basic idea on what the book is about, but what <i>actually happens</i> in this book? To which I say: nothing. That's right, don't pay attention to the summary they give to this book - it's all lies! Sure they give us an actually <i>interesting</i> premise to go by - but they don't do anything with it until the very end of the book. I felt that Despain just left it towards the big "climatic" scenes, where we were all are meant to be like: "Oh my g</span>
  <span id="freeText4517882892840160594" style="display:none"><b>In a Nuthsell:</b> You may be asking: alright, so I've got a fairly basic idea on what the book is about, but what <i>actually happens</i> in this book? To which I say: nothing. That's right, don't pay attention to the summary they give to this book - it's all lies! Sure they give us an actually <i>interesting</i> premise to go by - but they don't do anything with it until the very end of the book. I felt that Despain just left it towards the big "climatic" scenes, where we were all are meant to be like: "Oh my goodness! I am totally and absolutely awestruck by this apparent reveal which was just ignored all of this time for complete plot fodder and wankery!"<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380345510ra/700110.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Yeah well, some of us just <i>weren't</i>, alright?<br><br>Now, before I continue - I just wanted to say the worst thing about this book - like many others - is that this book had <i>potential</i> to be great. I mean, the whole freaking premise was about Grace meeting with an old friend, whom her family (especially her bland and annoying-ass older brother Jude) banished from their lives. Grace assumes this has something to do with the night Daniel disappeared, and (an unconscious) Jude was found on their front porch covered in a pool of his own blood.<br><br>But we don't get into that. Oh no, what we get instead is a whole book about Grace reunited with a childhood friend (and crush) - and how they plumment into this instantaneous, vapid kind of romance which is masquerading as this beautiful, intense, deep and doomed 'true love'. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Oh, did I forget to mention that Daniel is also a werewolf? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> And more tedious and boring nothingness ensures.<br><br>Some of you may complain and say that isn't good enough. I agree, but I argue that because this book is so painstakingly <b>dull</b> and hardly anything happens in this book - I didn't take that much away from it. Sure, it may not compel me into a violent rage the same way <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6752378.City_of_Fallen_Angels__The_Mortal_Instruments___4_" title="City of Fallen Angels (The Mortal Instruments, #4) by Cassandra Clare" rel="nofollow noopener">City of Fallen Angels</a> might, but if I were to compare this to every other YA paranormal book I've read - yeah, it's pretty damn forgettable.<br><br><b>Plot or the <i>lack</i> of one and other Writing Stuff</b><br>While I was reading this book, the only constant thought I had was: <b>WHY IS NOTHING HAPPENING IN THIS BOOK?</b><br><br>And yes, I do include the supposedly "climatic" battle near the end of the book. Climatic, my butt. It was just rushed, and very light of action. The ending was pretty unsatisfactory because it was trying to raise more questions and open more loose threads in order to have <b>some</b> sort of sequel bait, which I will not be lured into. Nope, I will not touch the rest of this 'series' with a ten foot pole. <s>Unless I was trying to <i>beat it to death</i>.</s> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I also, sure as hell do not buy into the deux ex machina ending of Daniel being saved because Grace saved him through "the magical powers of love". I'm sorry, but after seeing it in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3975774.Evermore__The_Immortals___1_" title="Evermore (The Immortals, #1) by Alyson Noel" rel="nofollow noopener">Evermore</a> and a whole load of other books (aside from Harry Potter. At least THAT made some sense...?) butcher this concept and took it to level of stupid never seen before- I will not be taken into this bullshit. Bree Despain, I want a more substanial explanation to why Daniel was 'cured' and I want it now! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Not only was this book ridiciulously slow-paced, but I felt like the plot was so all over the place that even the <i>book</i> didn't know what exactly it was about either. Was it going to be about a tragically doomed romance with werewolves thrown in there because we can? Or conflict between Grace, Jude and Daniel - who clearly has not let the past go and have a lot of issues to tackle? Was it going to be a murder mystery, and did the Markham monster really exist?<br><br>What I seem to get was a non-existent plot, and we read nothing about Grace going to and from school/home, being indescisive about hanging out with Daniel or not, her half-assed romance with him and... nothing else really. I think the only VAGUELY interesting thing was the whole agenda Jude had against him/why he hated Daniel so much.<br><br>I know this cannot be just me, but did every <i>single</i> scene have to come under some stupid and asinine subheading? Really, because it wasn't like you could have just TOLD US in the story that it was 'four years ago' or 'later that morning'. <br><br>Did you think that we were that dumb that we wouldn't be able to figure this out on our own, Despain? Did you?<br><br>In short, my problem with this book was that it was so BORING. I swear that you could just cut the entire <i>first half</i> of this book out and you would lose <b>
  <i>nothing</i>
</b>. Now, if the book wanted to really grab my interest, I figured that the book should have started just a bit before the first murder of the victim <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Maryanne <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and bring more forshadowing to the whole werewolf thing and... stuff.<br><br>Don't even get me started on the whole mythology. While it was interesting, it had a pretty heavy religious tone which seemed just awkwardly shoved in at the last minute (after Daniel explains what he is, etc) and it is so under developed, that I was pretty sure that you could cut out the paranormal aspect, and it would change nothing in this book.<br><br>Also the heavily religious and smug moral self-righteousness tone to this book was just jarring and annoying. Just saying.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380345510ra/700111.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><b>Protagonist: Grace Divine</b><br>Most of the characters were just inane, boring and completely irrelevant. I mean, sure - Grace's father and Daniel (to a some extent) <i>may</i> are less annoying than everyone else, but in the long run, am I going to remember these stock characters in a year? Six months? Even two hours later down the track?<br><br>I think Grace is the worst case of this, because we are generally seeing this through HER eyes and HER perspective and so it is HER that we have to spend the most time with.<br><br>There really is nothing remarkable about her. She just comes off as your generic lovestruck and oh so selfless/caring heroine who cannot think for herself in these YA paranormal books. I mean I'm fine with her "good traits" but there was NOTHING else to her - she was just so bland and is like one of those characters who are just THERE for the sake of being the main (mostly male) protagonist's love interest. I mean the way she reacts to everything makes me believe the author was trying <i>really</i> hard to make her some overt incarnate of absolute goodness. <br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Like take the moment when Daniel infodumps to her about him being a werewolf urbat thing - and she goes home to think over it. Now what Daniel has is a hereditary thing, so I don't know where Grace gets the right to be so sorrowful and blaming <i>herself</i> for it. Is SHE his mother? No (well I hope not and this isn't some River Song/Melody Pond/Elaine and Martin McFly thing because that would be just... creepy). So where did she get this notion that <i>she</i> had anything to do with it? Self-absorbed, much? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>One other thing that really bugs me about her is the fact that she is just a blank slate. She has <b>
  <i>no</i>
</b> personality or opinions of her own whatsoever and is just so goddamn gullible. When Daniel was yapping on to her about the whole urbat nonesense - she just believes him straightaway, no denial or rationalizing it and certainly doesn't do any research to cross reference and to see if Daniel wasn't just you know, lying off his ass or just plain <i>crazy</i>. Honestly, and you call yourself a <i>nerdy grade-A student</i>? I SCOFF AT YOU AND YOUR DELUSIONS! <br><br>Also her abundant wholesomeness and naivety either really irritates or scares the flying hell out of me. Seriously, you are a fairly educated and supposedly intelligent person - you <i>cannot</i> be this goddamn oblivious and stupid. It's like she attended the Clary Fray Online Course on how to be a stupid protagonist or something.<br><br><b>An Example of Grace's Shining Moment of either Pure Obliviousness or Just Plain Stupid</b><br><br><i>Before I knew it, I was in what I presumed was [Daniel's] bedroom. <br><br>Little tingling pricks ran up my spine.<br><br>It looked like someone had been keeping a large dog in this closet/room. The door was marred by several claw-like glashes -- like the way Daisy would leave scratches on my bedroom door when I left her home alon, only these scratches were much larger and deeper. The door frame was splintered and cracked. Whatever animal had been kept in here had apparently gotten out.</i> - pg. 65<br><br><b>My reaction:</b> ...<br><br>WHAT THE FLYING MONKEYS IS WRONG WITH YOU, GRACE? <b>
  <i>GET THE HELL OUT OF THERE!</i>
</b> CAN'T YOU SEE HE COULD BE SOME KIND OF CRAZY SERIAL KILLER? WHAT MORE DO YOU WANT? ANIMAL SACRIFICES HANGING FROM THE WALL? <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380345510ra/700112.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>You know, it took me a while to figure out - but apparently Grace has violet eyes. <b>
  <i>Really</i>
</b> now, Despain? As far as I am concerned, the only person I allow to have such an oddity (that I can think off the top of my head) is Alanna <br><br>from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8596.Tamora_Pierce" title="Tamora Pierce" rel="nofollow noopener">Tamora Pierce</a>'s <u>Song of the Lioness Quartet</u> series - because she is an actual awesomely kick-ass heroine. Grace is not. Grace is a gullible, soulless little idiot with no personality. Your argument is invalid, Despain. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380345510ra/700113.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Main Love Interest: Daniel</b><br>Now Daniel, I had pretty mixed feelings about. In the beginning, I was ready and willing to instantly hate this guy. He was just a conceited jerface and I sure as hell didn't buy into his or Grace being "artistic" and having a deep passion for "art". I just thought this was just the author trying to make them deep, substanial and less threatening characters (in Daniel's case) with intellectual prowress without actually, you know, <i>showing</i> it. <br><br>Also, a message to not only to this book, but to a good chunk of YA Paranormal books. CAN WE PLEASE STOP HAVING OUR PROTAGONIST BEING INCREDIBLY GOOD ARTISTS/READERS IF YOU ARE NOT WILLING TO BACK IT UP? Honestly, I don't care how much Clary/Dru/Bella/Luce/every other twit likes to "read all the great classics" or has a great knack for drawing or something equally stupid, just STOP IT IF IT CONTRIBUTES NOTHING TO CHARACTER OR PLOT. <br><br>Suddenly, Daniel pulls a fast Heel Face Turn and I don't even notice nor care - because at that point, I was just grateful for <i>anything</i> to happen in the 'dark and deep abyss of nothingness' that this book is drowning in.<br><br>However, when I read more about his backstory: what with the whole neglected, abusive childhood he had to endure, and seeking solace and comfort in believing he found a real family with Grace's... I found that there was potential to actually develop Daniel's character - and you start to feel a <i>bit</i> sympathetic towards him. Okay maybe mine was in equal mass to <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mole_%28unit%29" rel="nofollow noopener">Avagadro's number</a>, but still! <br><br>But then this idiot has pull the all Edward Cullens/Jace Wayland whining act and says, "oh stay away from me! I don't know if I can resist ravaging you if you keep invading my personal space and just back away - because I AM PURE EEEEEEEEEEEEEVIL!" but he goes ahead and does this:<br><br><i>"You drive me crazy!" Daniel shouted at my back. He paused for a moment. "I just wanted to show you," he said, his tone much softer.</i> - pg. 107<br><br>Dude, anyone who can change their moods that fast is someone you should be very, very afraid of and actually take his word - you stay away from him and call the cops/Ghostbusters/nearest paranormal creature hunter!<br><br><b>Main Romance: Grace/Daniel</b><br>What can I say about this relationship? It was equally stupid and boring as the people involved in it. Like the plot, there was actual conflict and issue to help, I don't know - <i>develop and strengthen</i> their growing romance! Think about it: they had an actual past together, there is obvious some issue between Daniel/Jude that they need to overcome/find out and they could actually explore the "I love you but we should not be together because I am most likely to kill you" aspect of their supposedly 'tragic' romance. Yeah, believe me honey, when I say the only thing tragic about it was that it ever happened.<br><br>Also, it may be just me but I got some weird <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3473.A_Walk_to_Remember" title="A Walk to Remember by Nicholas Sparks" rel="nofollow noopener">A Walk to Remember</a>/<a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beauty_and_the_Beast_%281991_film%29" rel="nofollow noopener">Beauty and the Beast</a> vibe from their romance. I think it was that undertone that Daniel can be saved/redeemed if he had a girl like Grace to fix/change him! I think it was because Despain placed such a big fat emphasis on how only Grace could save him and how pure/good/sweet/innocent/selfless/caring/insert some other nauseating fluffy adjective here she was and how wronged/tragic/angsty Daniel was, it seemed to be the only conclusion to it! Or something...<br><br>Overall, don't pick this book up. Unless you really, really mean to read it.<br><br><b>Recommended for:</b> no one. Okay maybe the Twilight/A Walk to Remember crowd...<br><b>Rating:</b> 1/5 stars</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="4517882892840160594" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_80931042" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/80931042" />
    <a title="Amy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2874225-amy"><img alt="Amy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599974197p2/2874225.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/80931042?book_show_action=true">Dec 13, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy" href="/user/show/2874225-amy">Amy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2874225-amy?shelf=ya-ya-ya">ya-ya-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2874225-amy?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer80931042" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10276562257203618654">THE DARK DIVINE was one of the best debut books I've read this year. It could probably even be the best. This one was a real page-turner. <br/> <br/>At first glance, the story is your typical paranormal romance. But whereas many of the YA paranormal romance books out there these days fall flat on their faces when it comes to the characters and the plot, this one does not. Bree Despain really knows how to create her characters, and give them personalities that make them shine. Or well, not necessarily shin</span>
  <span id="freeText10276562257203618654" style="display:none">THE DARK DIVINE was one of the best debut books I've read this year. It could probably even be the best. This one was a real page-turner. <br /> <br />At first glance, the story is your typical paranormal romance. But whereas many of the YA paranormal romance books out there these days fall flat on their faces when it comes to the characters and the plot, this one does not. Bree Despain really knows how to create her characters, and give them personalities that make them shine. Or well, not necessarily shine, but make them believable and enthralling to read about.<br /><br />Daniel was a great character. He's more of the bad boy type than not, but because of so, he was really appealing. He's conflicted but there's a reason, and I loved the relationship between him and Grace. Their interactions were really wonderful...they were actually credible and the scenes that were meant to be romantic were beautiful. Despain tells her story in such a way that made me eager for any Grace-Daniel scenes. I loved how there were reasons for Grace and Daniel's love for each other, and how it wasn't just infatuation-at-first-sight. (Like in Fallen, Evermore, and Twilight...) <br /><br />I loved how family played a big part in the story, and how there was a set of diverse characters that made the mystery in this book authentic, and kept me guessing at who the baddy was until the end! <br /> <br />And the plot...wow. Unlike many other paranormal romances, there was actually a plot in this story! An intriguing plot with a mystery that was slowly revealed, bit by bit and hint by hint, over the course of the story. This made the story really addicting...I couldn't stop reading! It was evidently well-researched and well-developed, making for a solid plot with heart-pounding scenes.<br /><br />Despain's take on the paranormal in THE DARK DIVINE was really, really good. The paranormal being in her story is very often used, but I think Despain's version ranks among the best. It's solidly constructed and has a legitimate and interesting history behind it.<br /><br />I honestly don't know how to give this book a review worthy of its content. There was so much going on, and a lot of factors contributing to the plot that made it really enticing, but I can't give them away without spoiling it, so I won't! There are little things that you read about in the beginning that come together in the end in a satisfying and sweet conclusion, but all the same, I am desperately awaiting the sequel. Overall, a beautiful book with a beautiful story! </span>
  <a data-text-id="10276562257203618654" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2401865-sab-h-ya-bliss?shelf=own">own</a>,

<span id="freeTextContainer9409687099337863218">More like 3.5 stars.<br/><br/>I was so exited about this book! I think I was too exited. Ballads of Suburbia is a hard book to follow, I kept thinking about it long after I was supposed to be into this one. This book was not awfully trapping. Even though I really liked the romance part, I didn't feel so much the supernatural. I didn't quite feel the edge or the mystery. She waited to long to explain what was going on. The writing was awkward, some dialogs seemed to be not believable.<br/><br/>The plot is unsteady. </span>
  <span id="freeText9409687099337863218" style="display:none">More like 3.5 stars.<br /><br />I was so exited about this book! I think I was too exited. Ballads of Suburbia is a hard book to follow, I kept thinking about it long after I was supposed to be into this one. This book was not awfully trapping. Even though I really liked the romance part, I didn't feel so much the supernatural. I didn't quite feel the edge or the mystery. She waited to long to explain what was going on. The writing was awkward, some dialogs seemed to be not believable.<br /><br />The plot is unsteady. I know its an 'uncorrected' ARC, but sometimes I wanted to stop reading it; and then other times, and here's the contradiction: I was trapped by the romance. She did a wonderful job making the love story yummy. What I liked the most was the ending, it will be great to see how the story goes on.<br /><br />I've discovered while discussing this book, that I may have a dislike tendency for good girls as main characters. I tend to prefer bad-ass dangerous -Katniss/Katsa style- main characters. Grace is goodness personified, as the child of a pastor would be. To me, she was dull and boring (though Bella fans may find the appeal, I'm not a Bella fan myself) I did like Daniel a lot and Jude too.<br /><br />I obviously have to mention the cover was absolutely beautiful and intriguing. I loved it since I first saw it. It brought my attention and curiosity to the book, that's a good thing. Then again, after reading it, I have no idea how it may have any connection to the story. None. Still, it is an interesting read for those of you who enjoy love story/supernatural. If you liked Evermore you'll enjoy this one too.</span>

<div id="review_97008620" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/97008620" />
    <a title="Thomas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas"><img alt="Thomas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567953607p2/2018505.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/97008620?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas">Thomas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer97008620" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14877323128040344864">Grace Divine is bossy, rebellious, stubborn, and yet a total good girl - after all, she is the daughter of the local pastor. Her life is filled with homey family dinners and study groups at the library, until long lost Daniel Kalbi returns. Daniel is exactly as Grace remembers him: edgy, aesthetic, and yet mysteriously attractive. As Grace gets pulled deeper and deeper into his world, she finds herself face to face with the terrifying secret he's been hiding from her all along.<br/><br/>There's a reason w</span>
  <span id="freeText14877323128040344864" style="display:none">Grace Divine is bossy, rebellious, stubborn, and yet a total good girl - after all, she is the daughter of the local pastor. Her life is filled with homey family dinners and study groups at the library, until long lost Daniel Kalbi returns. Daniel is exactly as Grace remembers him: edgy, aesthetic, and yet mysteriously attractive. As Grace gets pulled deeper and deeper into his world, she finds herself face to face with the terrifying secret he's been hiding from her all along.<br /><br />There's a reason why my summary of the story is so short: to reveal absolutely anything about the plot would be a huge mistake! The best thing about <i>The Dark Divine</i> was the pace of the plot: it was fast but not too fast, and held my interest long enough for me to finish it in a day. Despain writes well and did a nice job with mixing the paranormal and religious aspects of the book; very smooth juxtaposition and it fit well with the characterization of Grace.<br /><br />My one complaint concerns the relationship between Grace and Daniel. It just wasn't believable enough; sometimes the passion was there, like during the end of the book, but most of the time I was thinking," wait, how did you guys fall in love again?" Overall, their romance was a bit too shallow and far-fetched.<br /><br />For the most part I really loved <i>The Dark Divine</i>. Hopefully readers will be able to see Grace and Daniel's bond strengthen and progress in the next book of the series, <i>The Lost Saint</i>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14877323128040344864" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_100958009" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/100958009" />
    <a title="Desperado" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3422821-desperado"><img alt="Desperado" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487999118p2/3422821.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/100958009?book_show_action=true">May 02, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Desperado" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Desperado" href="/user/show/3422821-desperado">Desperado</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3422821-desperado?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3422821-desperado?shelf=paranormal-ya">paranormal-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3422821-desperado?shelf=reviews">reviews</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer100958009" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4672276863593053776">My Thoughts:<br/><br/>I'm going to try my best to write this review without spoilers which is gonna be difficult given this book is mainly about Daniel's "secret".<br/><br/>Anyway,Grace is the daughter of a pastor & stepford wife-esque mother. She also has three siblings; a younger sister, older brother, & baby brother. When she was younger, she & her older brother were close to a neighborhood kid Daniel which ended abruptly when he disappeared the night her older brother (Jude) came home beat up to all hell. Years</span>
  <span id="freeText4672276863593053776" style="display:none">My Thoughts:<br /><br />I'm going to try my best to write this review without spoilers which is gonna be difficult given this book is mainly about Daniel's "secret".<br /><br />Anyway,Grace is the daughter of a pastor &amp; stepford wife-esque mother. She also has three siblings; a younger sister, older brother, &amp; baby brother. When she was younger, she &amp; her older brother were close to a neighborhood kid Daniel which ended abruptly when he disappeared the night her older brother (Jude) came home beat up to all hell. Years later Daniel reappears in their podunk town out of the blue &amp; the mystery begins.<br /><br />On to my thoughts. Throughout this novel I debated whether to give it 2 stars or 3. There were chapters where I felt 2 stars were too generous. The concept for this novel has been recycled billions of times but there were a few twists (&amp; the author's viewpoint based on her mormon background) that saved this novel from paranormal YA mediocrity. I enjoyed the lore surrounding the mystery. I enjoyed the family &amp; friendship dynamics. I enjoyed our teen hero Daniel. I even enjoyed the religious aspect although I felt like it was being shoved down my throat a few times. What I didn't enjoy was our heroine, Grace. She annoyed the crap out of me. Grace has this irritating need to fix people which often comes off as intrusive. What makes it more annoying is that she isn't doing it so much out of the goodness of her heart as to rationalize her own feelings. For example, she would bring food &amp; clothes over to Daniel &amp; tell herself it was because she was such a good christian &amp; living up to her name. In actuality it was so she could be near him. It would be cute if she didn't come off as holier-than-thou. She also was very childish &amp; naive for someone who is almost 17. One second she loved Daniel &amp; thought Jude was a liar. The next she hated Daniel &amp; couldn't believe she didn't listen to her brother. She was all over the freaking place &amp; it stayed that way until nearly the end of the book. I tried my hardest to like her but the second I felt something more than intense dislike, she'd do something stupid that put her back on my TSTL list.<br /><br />Overall, I think I would've enjoyed this novel alot more if it wasn't told exclusively from the heroine's view. It doesn't really break new ground &amp; comes off as cliche.<b>But</b> I did find some parts of this novel entertaining. I might even read the next in the series (yes its a part of a series. Seems like every freaking book these days is a part of a series) in the hopes that Grace redeems herself &amp; grows a brain/backbone.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4672276863593053776" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_55232659" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/55232659" />
    <a title="Steph Su" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2010935-steph-su"><img alt="Steph Su" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1504243050p2/2010935.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/55232659?book_show_action=true">May 07, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steph Su" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steph Su" href="/user/show/2010935-steph-su">Steph Su</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2010935-steph-su?shelf=cover-lust">cover-lust</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2010935-steph-su?shelf=debs10">debs10</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer55232659" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13086562121797496334">THE DARK DIVINE is an interesting but ultimately underwhelming read that will still be eagerly embraced by paranormal romance fans of Twilight, Shiver, and other similar books.<br/><br/>The best thing about THE DARK DIVINE was the way it rewrote the typical werewolf story and infused it with history, magic, religion, and the balance of good and evil. It gave depth to Daniel’s werewolf character. I’m not a big werewolf girl, nor am I religious, but I enjoyed the way the two unexpectedly intertwined and enh</span>
  <span id="freeText13086562121797496334" style="display:none">THE DARK DIVINE is an interesting but ultimately underwhelming read that will still be eagerly embraced by paranormal romance fans of Twilight, Shiver, and other similar books.<br /><br />The best thing about THE DARK DIVINE was the way it rewrote the typical werewolf story and infused it with history, magic, religion, and the balance of good and evil. It gave depth to Daniel’s werewolf character. I’m not a big werewolf girl, nor am I religious, but I enjoyed the way the two unexpectedly intertwined and enhanced one another in this book.<br /><br />Unfortunately, the characters were for me rather difficult to connect with, as most of them felt like types I’ve read many times before. Grace was an extremely passive protagonist who elicited little sympathy from me. The tension between Grace’s parents often felt forced and unexplained. Daniel started out as stereotypical, but as the plot finally built and his background was finally revealed, he turned into a much more believable character.<br /><br />As for the romance, it felt like one that I’ve read many times before: good girls feels undeniable attraction with bad boy, who acts like a jerk initially but actually reciprocates the feelings, and True Love Ends Happily Ever After. The familiarity of the course of the romance was unimpressive and rather disappointing to me.<br /><br />The plot was rather infuriatingly slow, which may put off more impatient readers, but it does eventually build into an exciting paranormal world with an action-packed, heart-stopping ending. It does take an inventive writer to pull off what Bree Despain has as the ending, and I found it believable, heart-stopping, and satisfying. Overall, THE DARK DIVINE was perhaps not the book for me, but fans of Twilight-esque true love paranormal romances will find it a great addition to the genre.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13086562121797496334" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_61592005" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/61592005" />
    <a title="Krista (Miura Haruma-san, I will always miss you)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2082345-krista-miura-haruma-san-i-will-always-miss-you"><img alt="Krista (Miura Haruma-san, I will always miss you)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1436762808p2/2082345.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/61592005?book_show_action=true">Jun 29, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Krista (Miura Haruma-san, I will always miss you)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Krista (Miura Haruma-san, I will always miss you)" href="/user/show/2082345-krista-miura-haruma-san-i-will-always-miss-you">Krista (Miura Haruma-san, I will always miss you)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2082345-krista-miura-haruma-san-i-will-always-miss-you?shelf=own-ab">own-ab</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2082345-krista-miura-haruma-san-i-will-always-miss-you?shelf=best-character-s">best-character-s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2082345-krista-miura-haruma-san-i-will-always-miss-you?shelf=read-around">read-around</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2082345-krista-miura-haruma-san-i-will-always-miss-you?shelf=want-to-own">want-to-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2082345-krista-miura-haruma-san-i-will-always-miss-you?shelf=tears">tears</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2082345-krista-miura-haruma-san-i-will-always-miss-you?shelf=werewolves">werewolves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2082345-krista-miura-haruma-san-i-will-always-miss-you?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer61592005" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8250988267897994431">I was really looking forward to this book, and although it did not disappoint me, it also wasn't quite what I'd expected. I knew what it was that Daniel had done from the very first time I read the inside flap of the book. I thought perhaps my assumption was wrong, because it felt too obvious, but nope...it's really obvious what happened between Daniel and Jude.<br/>The twist wasn't surprising either. I guessed it about halfway through, though it wasn't near as obvious as the "mysterious" event that </span>
  <span id="freeText8250988267897994431" style="display:none">I was really looking forward to this book, and although it did not disappoint me, it also wasn't quite what I'd expected. I knew what it was that Daniel had done from the very first time I read the inside flap of the book. I thought perhaps my assumption was wrong, because it felt too obvious, but nope...it's really obvious what happened between Daniel and Jude.<br />The twist wasn't surprising either. I guessed it about halfway through, though it wasn't near as obvious as the "mysterious" event that made Daniel disappear. <br /><br />The characters were...well, lets just say some were well done and others were not. The role Grace's parents played was pretty solid, and I could definitely see them as real people. As for her "friend" April...What was up with that girl? She was SUCH a flimsy character, hardly a friend at all. Why is it that Grace is so supposedly popular and has had quite a few boyfriends, yet she has only one friend who really isn't her friend at all. <br /><br />Also, the teeny tiny minor characters, like the "mean girls" seemed totally pointless to me with their one-liners. <br />Then there was Jude. I don't know why so many people like him. I just found him extremely irritating. He was supposedly this "great guy," yet not once in the entire book does he act the part. <br />I know he supposedly has a "reason," but said reason should not have affected his personality so much. I mean, he was an annoying jerk. ANd whiny. What 17-year-old is so freakin' whiny? He was more of a baby than baby James!<br />It was all "Oh, boo hoo hoo! The evil Daniel came back and he betrayed me so I'm going to make everyone around me miserable and act like a total brat! Boo Hoo Hoo!!!!!" Ugh, I was seriously tempted to dive through the book and slap that guy across the face. YES, he had reason to be angry at Daniel, but so what? I mean, it was supposed to be Daniel who was the major "bad guy" in Jude's mind...but what did he think he was acting like? A nice, forgiving guy? No! He scared Grace more than Daniel did!<br /><br />Now, for the reason I won't say, Jude has an excuse for acting out of character, but EVEN considering said reason, he still acted like a jerk. Not once in the book did he do anything remotely redeeming. Maybe in the memories of when they were younger Jude was more likable, but I just wish I could have seen more of that in the current time. <br />Grace herself...at times I liked her...others I didn't. She really wasn't THAT strong. She let everyone else make her decisions for her. <br />The second she found out what Daniel had done, she turned her back on him and told him to leave for good--not because she wanted to, but because she felt like she HAD to, because she owed it to the stupid, annoying Jude, her beloved 17 going on 7-year-old BIG brother!!! <br />Maybe it's just me, because I don't have any siblings so I don't know what it's like, but I don't see how Jude's anger and despair is justified. <br />Yes, his friend "betrayed" him, but why should Daniel's return give Jude the right to act like the king of the world and suddenly start telling everyone what to do and to feel sorry for him etc... And all of a sudden he starts dating April, who he'd barely spoken to before? Gee, I wonder if he did that to get sympathy and have someone to bad-mouth Daniel to??? I can't guess.<br />And then how he acts at the end? All sulky and sullen and "Oh my life's over and no one else could possibly understand and blah blah blah!" <br />Okay, so I'll stop picking on Jude now. I think it's pretty clear how I feel about him. <br /><br />About Daniel...well, I think it should be obvious by now how totally awesome I think he is! <br />For him, my sympathy ran deep. Every time I learned about what had happened to him or how he felt I just wanted to cry (usually did). He felt real to me. What was so great about him was that he was far from perfect. I despise "perfect" characters that don't have flaws and never make mistakes and just seem too good to be true. Daniel felt real, while still managing to stay completely likable. I love the way he talked about art. It made ME want to draw and paint and that's something I NEVER do!<br /><br />I loved the way he was with Grace. Some people may call it corny, but I thought it was just brilliant. I love how he was introduced by taking her art supplies then asking for a kiss for their return and then in the memory he did pretty much the same thing, So cute!<br />His love for Grace and her love for Daniel felt real, believable. I like the change of having him be both new and old. She'd known him almost forever, but then he disappeared--and now he's back. The whole "new guy/girl" routine is wearing thin, and this book managed to avoid that cliche. <br /><br />As for the story itself? It felt rushed. The supernatural aspect was explained well, but felt a bit scattered, disconnected. It didn't feel all that real or "plausible" to me. <br />As for what Grace had to do to "save" Daniel...I liked that idea alot. It was very unique. <br /><br />The ending was a little hectic and kind of annoying. What happened to Grace...well, it could go either way. Despain could make something good out of it, but as for Jude and what he did? I hope she's planning on bringing him back and having his character grow. <br /><br />I also felt bad for Don Mooney. Won't say why, but his ending was sad, though he did manage to prove himself. <br /><br />One thing I wondered about was how much Grace's mother knew about Daniel. That was unclear to me. Did she know his secret? I suppose she must have, though she didn't act as if she did.<br /><br />But the final scene was uplifting and made me both smile and cry, so that was well done. <br /><br />One question, though. If April saw everything that happened at the end, she now knows Daniel's secret, but this is not addressed for some reason. Is April really trustworthy enough to keep such a big secret? How will she react?<br />I want more, but I'm also a bit nervous. This book has its creepy points, and I don't know how much further it will go with that.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8250988267897994431" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_80359971" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/80359971" />
    <a title="Kater Cheek" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/611031-kater-cheek"><img alt="Kater Cheek" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442522034p2/611031.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/80359971?book_show_action=true">Dec 08, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kater Cheek" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kater Cheek" href="/user/show/611031-kater-cheek">Kater Cheek</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer80359971&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer80359971" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3845508798622792818">Got this as an advance review copy when I was in Philadelphia last month. I'm usually a sucker for YA novels--in my opinion, the standards for YA are much higher than for adult, so you're more likely to get a readable story. (Also, it has the most gorgeous cover I've seen in years.)<br/><br/>The novel started out so strongly that I thought it was going to be a must-read for everyone (I don't know when the release date is). We have a kind of unusual triangle between a sister, Grace, who loves her brother J</span>
  <span id="freeText3845508798622792818" style="display:none">Got this as an advance review copy when I was in Philadelphia last month. I'm usually a sucker for YA novels--in my opinion, the standards for YA are much higher than for adult, so you're more likely to get a readable story. (Also, it has the most gorgeous cover I've seen in years.)<br /><br />The novel started out so strongly that I thought it was going to be a must-read for everyone (I don't know when the release date is). We have a kind of unusual triangle between a sister, Grace, who loves her brother Jude and wants to be loyal to him, but is also captivated by Daniel, who used to be their neighbor and friend until Grace's family adopted him. Something happened years ago, something bad, and since then, no one mentions Daniel's name. Daniel is quite dark and Byronic, mysterious and a little dangerous. He hangs out with bad people, gets into passionate rages, and pisses off her parents when Grace mentions his name. In short, she is the guy every teenage girl secretly dreams of. Except that Grace is a good, obedient, and honest girl, so she tries to manipulate her family into accepting Daniel into their lives again.<br /><br />At first I found it refreshing that Grace was such a good kid. Obedient to parents, dutiful with house work, attentive to her studies, etc. I also quietly applauded how well the author managed tension. Despain managed to withhold just enough information from Grace (and us) to make us desperate to find out more. After all, some very important information had been withheld from Grace, namely, what did Daniel do to make him persona non grata in her family? We already know that Grace's father forgave Don, a guy who threatened to kill him, so what could Daniel have done that was that much worse?<br /><br />What started out as very promising got sluggish in the middle, as Grace's introspection wore me down. I wanted her to shut up with her inner turmoil and just get on with it. Eventually, it picked up again, and rather briskly rolled towards the ending. I thought the description of how Don played into the family dynamics was a little rushed, and at some point she comes across a series of letters that were meant to illuminate the entire mythology, but ended up kind of boring and confusing me with uninteresting characters I cared nothing for, and I lost whatever explaination they were meant to provide.<br /><br />I liked the ending, and found it satisfying. A few things bothered me, but they might not bother everyone. One, homeopathy as werewolf cure? It's just as implausible in the mythical world as it is in ours. Two, usually if you stab someone with a knife, they're <b>dead</b> but the characters don't believe that. And three (this is the big one for me) I really didn't like the Christian aspect of it. On one hand, it's fine if Grace is a goody-goody. On the other hand, the morals became more and more distinctly Christian as the book went along; they became less "do the right thing" and more "do what the bible tells you" which aren't the same.<br /><br />Church-going parents who want to hand their Twilight-loving daughters something they approve of should reach for this book. YA fans who are squicked out by religion should be forewarned.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3845508798622792818" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_76933722" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

<span id="freeTextContainer11909296901203329194">I received the ARC for The Dark Divine this week when our box of goodies came from Bree for being on her street team. I have to say, that I read the book in a day and I couldn't put it down. I was hooked when I read the first 17 pages here <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.breedespain.com/TDDsneakpeak.html'>http://www.breedespain.com/TDDsneakpe...</a>.<br/><br/>**This is SPOILER FREE**<br/>Grace Divine is part of a tight knit family, who help everyone they can, are do gooders in their community and hold no secrets, or so Grace thought. When a child hood friend, and someone who was </span>
  <span id="freeText11909296901203329194" style="display:none">I received the ARC for The Dark Divine this week when our box of goodies came from Bree for being on her street team. I have to say, that I read the book in a day and I couldn't put it down. I was hooked when I read the first 17 pages here <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.breedespain.com/TDDsneakpeak.html">http://www.breedespain.com/TDDsneakpe...</a>.<br /><br />**This is SPOILER FREE**<br />Grace Divine is part of a tight knit family, who help everyone they can, are do gooders in their community and hold no secrets, or so Grace thought. When a child hood friend, and someone who was once consider part of the family returns nothing will be the same.<br /><br />When Daniel returns, things start getting weird around Grace's town, and a dark Divine secret won't be kept secret for long. Grace and her close brother Jude's relationship becomes strained, her parents are hiding something from her and citizens in her town turn up dead. What evil is really lurking in her town? All things point to Daniel. Grace can't fight the pull and attraction she's always had for Daniel and since he's returned it's that much more intense. Even worse, her family has forbidden her to ever see him again after he left a couples years ago. There's something about him that Grace can't fight.<br /><br />Daniel is one tense character that you'll be so drawn to, you can't help but sucked into this story, as you want to know more about him and what he's hiding. Buckle up and enjoy the ride Bree takes you on as Grace is on a mission to make things right with her family, her town and with Daniel, but everything comes at a cost. Who's life will Grace's mission be to save? Not everyone is who you except them to be.<br /><br />This book is full of twists and turns and kept me glued to the book until I put it down. Nothing is what you except and the end will leave you wanting more. This hasn't been released yet and I'm already dying for the sequel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11909296901203329194" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer112098397" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer7642898109676166638">I felt that this was a book that did not need to be a paranormal romance. I thought the main topics of interest in the story came from the religious aspect and the idea of dark secrets in a family who are looked upon as truly divine. The love subplot and werewolf bits felt forced compared to the rest of the story, which wasn't brilliantly written, but certainly kept my interest for longer. The love plot was samey and nothing I've not read before in much better, more original books.<br/><br/>I was disappoi</span>
  <span id="freeText7642898109676166638" style="display:none">I felt that this was a book that did not need to be a paranormal romance. I thought the main topics of interest in the story came from the religious aspect and the idea of dark secrets in a family who are looked upon as truly divine. The love subplot and werewolf bits felt forced compared to the rest of the story, which wasn't brilliantly written, but certainly kept my interest for longer. The love plot was samey and nothing I've not read before in much better, more original books.<br /><br />I was disappointed that the book's heroine fell into so many of the pothols associated with paranormal YA heroines - she had a lot of interesting traits, certainly more than many other heroines, but they all seemed to be shoved aside the moment the love story came into it. She was also prone to making daft decisions and jumping to stupid conclusions. Daniel was okay but as I said earlier, I was just much more interested in other characters, especially Jude. Take away the paranormal element and write the story as a struggle to be righteous when you're anything but and I think that story would be much more interesting. <br /></span>

<div id="review_83092220" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <span id="freeText3735022824847101706" style="display:none">Far too message-laden (with Biblical teachings) and also tries too hard to escape from the very anger it seems to rail against; forgetting the ability to use "grace" in the face of intolerable betrayal. <div id="review_1543389656" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1543389656" />
    <a title="CeCe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10480068-cece"><img alt="CeCe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551369180p2/10480068.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1543389656?book_show_action=true">Feb 09, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="CeCe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="CeCe" href="/user/show/10480068-cece">CeCe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10480068-cece?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10480068-cece?shelf=friends-annoyed-me">friends-annoyed-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10480068-cece?shelf=borrowed-library">borrowed-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10480068-cece?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10480068-cece?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1543389656" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6221028788394354929">It was not a bad read. Likable characters. I liked the suspense. The heroine did not hide her feelings for the hero, but it never made her appear desperate or weak. She was honest and I just found it refreshing. She did not play games. <br/><br/>The heroine is daughter of a pastor. I was worried that her father was going to be a jerk, but he was not. In this book, he practiced what he preached. The mother was the irritating one. <br/><br/>Daniel comes back after three years of being gone. The last time Daniel was s</span>
  <span id="freeText6221028788394354929" style="display:none">It was not a bad read. Likable characters. I liked the suspense. The heroine did not hide her feelings for the hero, but it never made her appear desperate or weak. She was honest and I just found it refreshing. She did not play games. <br /><br />The heroine is daughter of a pastor. I was worried that her father was going to be a jerk, but he was not. In this book, he practiced what he preached. The mother was the irritating one. <br /><br />Daniel comes back after three years of being gone. The last time Daniel was seen was when Grace's brother, Jude, came home covered in his own blood. Grace has always loved Daniel, but Jude keeps telling her to stay away from him - that he is dangerous. There are a few surprises/twists. Most annoying character had to be Grace's BFF, April. I am not sure what her angle is yet. April is dating Jude, but I think she is only friends with Grace to get to her brother. April was odd.<br /><br />I have the second book, but I am not sure if I will read it. I will probably start it and see how it goes. </span>

          </span>

<div id="review_71397045" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/71397045" />
    <a title="~Tina~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2594672-tina"><img alt="~Tina~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411474324p2/2594672.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/71397045?book_show_action=true">Sep 16, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="~Tina~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="~Tina~" href="/user/show/2594672-tina">~Tina~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=wolves-shapeshiftes">wolves-shapeshiftes</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer71397045" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4676828431228300527">No doubt that we really have been blessed with a lot of brilliant YA paranormal novels this year and <b>The Dark Divine</b> is on that list!!<br/><br/>Grace's story starts off with a question. Why did Daniel just disappear? What made her friend, her brothers best friend and her childhood crush just up and leave 3 years ago?<br/>Daniel is back, and Grace is determined to fix it. For her brother, for Daniel, for herself, no matter what...<br/>How could she have possibly known of an ancient curse that has haunted the ones sh</span>
  <span id="freeText4676828431228300527" style="display:none">No doubt that we really have been blessed with a lot of brilliant YA paranormal novels this year and <b>The Dark Divine</b> is on that list!!<br /><br />Grace's story starts off with a question. Why did Daniel just disappear? What made her friend, her brothers best friend and her childhood crush just up and leave 3 years ago?<br />Daniel is back, and Grace is determined to fix it. For her brother, for Daniel, for herself, no matter what...<br />How could she have possibly known of an ancient curse that has haunted the ones she loves, that could destroy everything she ever knew existed.<br /><br /><b>The Dark Divine</b> Is an ingenious take, surrounding this particular paranormal element. I had no clue that this was what was lurking in the pages.<br />The plot is thickened with a lot of mystery and intrigue. Written in evenly paced events so we are learning with Grace as the story unfolds. <br />I found the history and secrets fascinating and I applaud the creativity and imagination's heart that went into it.<br /><br />The characters were very well written and well understood. Some really shocked me with the way the twist went.<br />Grace is very strong, good-nature, level headed and brave, it was easy to be proud of her.<br />Daniel is a beautiful mess. He's mysterious and torn, a very troubled soul that still wants to believe.<br /><br />There love story brings on a whole new meaning to Forbidden and it's that very reason why this book stands out.<br />Beautiful!<br /><br />I think the only struggle was the religious aspect in the story. I believe in God, but for some reason I always felt it odd to put him in a paranormal universe this in-depth. But when I look at the bigger picture I think it was necessary for this particular book, so I'm just pushing it aside. <br /><br />All in all this was an incredible story. There is more mystery then romance in this book, but It really worked in this case. It made it more believable and easy to relate too. It left enough room to make an easy sequel so I'm looking forward to finding out what happens next.<br /><br /><b>The Dark Divine</b> is a Fantastic debut that will keep you well entertained. It will challenge you to believe in True Love. And Fear True Loves First Kill...<br /><br />A Must Read!<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4676828431228300527" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('xGtlzQ0OBejR1QyMAzmWKEpLvEfdl4pR8Nb9UIQJjb/+TQwftlDMgHb+uO30zJz3nBRbjxMaBDarqLvhSUp/JQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('vOnfQHY+jIl3AW8FCxpUyurt3jufeGh43rROu79FcUiGz7aSzWBF4dAq22T8714VPLI581H15h+FyggKcgaD0g==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer14098818780631265809">The Short: Bree rediscovered her childhood love for creating stories when she took a semester off college to write and direct plays for at-risk, inner-city teens from Philadelphia and New York. She currently lives in Salt Lake City, Utah with her husband, two young sons, and her beloved TiVo. The Dark Divine is Bree's debut novel.<br/><br/>The Long: As a kid, Bree would staple folded papers to make her own </span>
  <span id="freeText14098818780631265809" style="display:none">The Short: Bree rediscovered her childhood love for creating stories when she took a semester off college to write and direct plays for at-risk, inner-city teens from Philadelphia and New York. She currently lives in Salt Lake City, Utah with her husband, two young sons, and her beloved TiVo. The Dark Divine is Bree's debut novel.<br /><br />The Long: As a kid, Bree would staple folded papers to make her own "novels." As a teen, she wrote stories in notebooks while her friends waited for the next page to be finished. Her teachers told her she should be a writer. But Bree thought only special people could be writers, so as the years past, she settled into the idea of becoming a lawyer or something else just as ordinary.<br /><br />Bree rediscovered her childhood love for creating stories when she took a semester off college to write and direct plays for at-risk, inner city teens from Philadelphia and New York. With a renewed passion for story, and the young adult audience, she returned to Brigham Young University, filled her schedule with creative writing and literature classes, and started writing stories again. But regular life kicked in, and she soon found herself married with a new baby, working full-time, and with very little writing done.<br /><br />That’s when the universe threw a pick-up truck in her path. The car accident left Bree with an understanding that life was too short to not do what you absolutely love. A few days later, her husband brought home a used laptop computer, placed it by her bedside, and said, “You’d better start writing.” Her life has never been the same since. <br /><br />In a moment of karmic perfection, Bree received the offer to purchase The Dark Divine on the 6th anniversary of the car accident that put her back on the path to becoming an author.</span>
